##### Nurturing Family Life in God's Fatherly Love

> Yet You are our Father, though Abraham does not know us and Israel does not acknowledge us. You, O Lord, are our Father; our Redeemer from Everlasting is Your name.

<< Isaiah 63:16

> Let all the wondrous influence you possess in forming your child and fixing his destiny be wielded for this one thing—to satisfy the desire of the Savior's heart, and make your child wholly His …. Dear parents! who have taken the Savior as your only teacher in the revelation of the mysteries of Divine love, let Him teach you the preciousness of your little ones. Learn to see in them what He does; in His light your care of them will become a blessing to yourself and to them.

<< Andrew Murray, *The Children for Christ*

###### Introduction

In this first session, we explore this fundamental principle: each parent's relationship with God as Father is hugely significant in sustaining, shaping, and energizing all parenting work. <Callout>Relationship with God best outfits us for our parenting vocation.</Callout> To know and enjoy God as loving Father is to equip ourselves to build Christian hearth and home. In Psalm 103:1–22, the Bible gives us a compelling picture of God's divine parental care toward his people. This biblical hymn of praise explicitly attests to and celebrates the fact that God treats his people like a loving father. Throughout the psalm, the author fleshes out specifics of how God cares for his people, inviting us to establish our lives—and parenting—in God's fatherly love. No father or mother can expect to care for their children—or build a godly home—without being sheltered, sustained, and supported by God's divine love for his people. It is under the coverage of divine compassion that our parental labors have divine power.

Christian homebuilding is an expression of a life of worship and devotion to God that is animated by God's fatherly love, sustained by God's divine care, and is established upon God's covenantal faithfulness. Where worship, devotion, piety, faith, and obedience have priority, childraising takes on a Christian character. If worship is the sturdy foundation of every healthy Christian home, it requires us as parents to cultivate our life with God. The business done in the home—which has a most important influence upon society—has its genesis in our walk with and worship of God. We neglect this foundation to our great peril and embrace it to our enduring joy!

###### All That Is Within Me: Being Captured by a Vision of God's Glorious Rule

The dominant refrain in Psalm 103 is "bless the Lord" (103:1; cf. 103:2, 20–22), an invitation to praise God for his character and work. This psalm—an uninhibited hymn of praise—extols God for his "holy name" (103:1) and his "kind deeds" (103:2). When the psalmist cries "O my soul" (103:1; cf. 103:2, 22), he shows us that genuine praise should come from the depths of our being—sincere adoration exclaimed from our inner person. God-honoring worship is also an act and attitude of wholehearted devotion, offering to God "all that is within me" (103:1). Such undivided resignation to the Lord shapes our focus and attention, making us careful to "not forget" (103:1; cf. 103:18) divine kindness in its many-sided array. The psalm tells us that God deserves worship from "all His angels mighty in strength" (103:20), "all His hosts" (103:21), and "all His works in all places" (103:22). God is worthy to be worshiped by all creation—animate and inanimate.

This psalm makes it clear that worship of God invigorates a life of piety and obedience. Genuine worship is more than verbal homage and energetic song. Those who truly worship God are his "servants" (103:21) who "carry out His word" (103:20), "hearken to the voice of His command" (103:20), and "do His will" (103:21). God's people are marked as "those who keep His covenant" (103:18), and those who "remember to obey His precepts" (103:18). The life of obedience comes from an underlying faith in God, made possible because God's people "fear Him" (103:11; cf. 103:13, 17). The fear of God moves God's people to submission, expressing their devotion as those who live under "His dominion" (103:22).

Every godly parent's hope and desire should be to establish their home on the foundation of worship. Worshiping families are marked by exuberant praise of God's worth, godly fear of God's majesty, humble obedience to God's commands, and willing submission under God's rule. Parents best lead their homes by regularly acknowledging God as King. Parental authority is only a derivative authority (an authority given by God) that seeks to use its own position and influence to direct its household under the safety of God's benevolent rule and reign. A godly home recognizes that "the Lord has established His throne in heaven, and His kingdom rules over all" (103:19) and earnestly seeks to make its household under this same benevolent rule.

<Callout>Parenting work is buoyed by a life of vibrant worship to the Lord.</Callout> This most basic and vital aspect of the Christian life—doxology—is the foundation of all godly parenting. To the extent our walk with the Lord is vibrant and sincere, our parenting vocation will be focused and fervent. Our lateral, human-to-human relationships with our children will only be as formative and meaningful as our vertical relationship is with the Lord.

Elevation of God's majesty is the best starting point for parental fidelity in the home. The home is a place to experience and recount God's peerless character and powerful deeds. <Callout>Childrearing is not ultimately a matter of deference to parental authority, but of fostering devotion to God.</Callout> A child's responsibility to honor and obey their parents is a means to inculcate a reverence to the ultimate authority, God himself. To raise children Godward is to raise children who will trust God in faith and serve him in obedience. Hearth-building and homebuilding are a matter of cultivating a family culture of worship, devotion, obedience, fear of God, and submission to God. To build our home in this way, in the end, is to have our home placed under God's merciful and compassionate dominion.

###### As a Father Has Compassion: Resting in the Fountain of God's Fatherly Love

In great detail, this psalm celebrates God's love for his people. God's love is compared to the love a father has toward his children: "as a father has compassion on his children, so the Lord has compassion on those who fear Him" (103:13). God's fatherly care for his people is best described as "loving devotion" (103:4; cf. 103:8, 11, 17)—a love that pledges itself to the well-being of another in covenant faithfulness. God's covenant love expresses itself in unwavering commitment and unconditional fidelity. It is love beyond emotion and sentiment. It is care galvanized by divine promise, divine trustworthiness, and divine relationship.

God's multifaceted love toward his people is further explained in this psalm. Showing tender care for his people, God's love is "compassionate" (103:8; cf. 103:13). Exhibiting redeeming kindness, God's love is "gracious" (103:8). Showing patience, God is "slow to anger" (103:8), showing mercy to repentant sinners (103:9–10). Emphasizing the depth of his divine care and the faithfulness to his people, the psalm testifies that God is "abounding in loving devotion" (103:8). God's love is wide, separating us from our sins "as far as the east is from the west" (103:12). God's love is immense: "as high as the heavens are above the earth, so great is His loving devotion for those who fear Him" (103:11). The immensity of God's love corresponds to its unending and eternal nature: "from everlasting to everlasting the loving devotion of the Lord extends to those who fear Him" (103:17).

Love is the heartbeat of parents toward their children. Although human parents cannot perfectly replicate divine love, <Callout>God's compassion for his people is the great pattern and power of all parental love.</Callout> When our love for our children takes the shape of God's paternal love for us, we can remain committed to our children regardless of the circumstances. We can discipline with faithfulness, clarity, and grace. We can provide what is best for our children without catering toward their unsanctified desires. We can call our children to self-control, self-restraint, and self-denial as an act of formation and not mere punishment. We can display self-sacrifice even when our children do not deserve it. Our love for our children will only be "right-sized" when it is God-shaped.

###### Crowned with Loving Devotion: Following the Pattern of God's Tender Care

God's fatherly and covenantal love is expressed in unparalleled divine care. The body of this psalm elaborates upon God's "kind deeds" (103:2) to his people (103:7). In his mercy, God "forgives all your iniquities" (103:3). His disciplining anger turns into divine pity for those who trust in him (103:9–10). More than just ignoring our sin, God has graciously "removed our transgressions from us" (103:12). In his power, he "heals all your diseases" (103:3). In his grace, he "redeems your life from the Pit" (103:4). In his covenant loyalty and fatherly care, he "crowns you with loving devotion and compassion" (103:4). In his benevolence and provision, God "satisfies you with good things, so that your youth is renewed like the eagle's" (103:5). In his moral perfection, he "executes righteousness and justice for all the oppressed" (103:6).

Parental care for their children should take the shape of God's love for his people. Parental authority that is domineering and manipulative is misshaped and malformed. Parents should express their love for their children in the way that God cares for his people. Exemplifying God's own loving devotion, godly parents display kindness, extend mercy, practice forgiveness, and show grace. Christian homes should be places of healing and little communities where divine redemption is enjoyed. Parents who experience God's loving devotion to his people can extend this to their progeny. Christian homebuilding should bask in God's good gifts with gratitude and foster an environment where compassion is amply shown. Christian families should cultivate biblical values of righteousness and justice, caring for the oppressed. In the end, collective parental care toward children is the expression of God's divine kindness that each parent has individually received.

God's covenant-keeping love is also gentle and sympathetic to his people. He knows that people are not like himself. God is fully aware of our finitude and limitations. The psalm tells us that God "knows our frame" and is "mindful that we are dust" (103:14). Certainly, humanity is noble and beautiful and "blooms like a flower of the field" (103:15). But the intrinsic dignity and splendor of humanity is tem- pered by its fleeting and passing life: "as for man, his days are like grass" (103:15) and after a short time "the wind passes over, it vanishes, and its place remembers it no more" (103:16). The grandeur that is every human life comes to an earthly end, usually sooner than we want. God not only tenderly cares for us in our limited and weak estate, but he extends over his people a covenant love that will never end: "from everlasting to everlasting the loving devotion of the Lord extends to those who fear Him" (103:17). God's fatherly love cares for his people in the fragility of the present life and for unending life to come.

<Callout>God's care for us is our model and means to care for our children.</Callout> Parents must be fully aware of children's weakness, limitations, and frailty. What a parent knows from years of life experience, a child has yet to understand. Child-raising requires patience, a God-given longsuffering to come alongside smaller and immature human beings to help them grow and mature. Children are resilient, but they are also fragile. The early years of a child's life are often most formative and shaping, impacting personhood, character, and values for many years to come. Modeled after God's own parental care for his people, a godly parent seeks for the home to be a garden, cultivated for each child to bloom and blossom into all that God created them to be. But most importantly, parental vocation must tend to the eternal nature of each and every child. Godly parents celebrate the dignity of each child, helping them to bloom into all that created them to be. But homebuilding that simply attempts to maximize the "bloom" of this temporary life amounts to parental neglect. The parent's greater task is to help each child find coverage under God's eternal loving devotion, a love that secures eternal life and unending relationship with God.

###### Those Who Keep His Covenant: Enjoying Relationship within God's Faithful Promises

If the parent's primary duty is to bring their children under God's everlasting covenant love, then they must learn how to guide their children into relationship with God. God establishes his relationship with his people in a covenant (103:18). In this covenant, God promises faithfulness to his people and summons his people to covenant faithfulness by trusting God and following his commands (103:17–18). This passage calls people to fear of God (103:11, 13, 17). This fear is a way of describing genuine faith: a deep reverence toward God and abiding trust in God that results in awe of and attachment to God. Those who have sincere faith in God will express their faith in obedience (103:18, 20–21). <Callout>Homebuilding in piety encouraging genuine faith in and earnest obedience to God—can have a generational impact</Callout> where God extends his righteousness "to their children's children" (103:17).

Godly parents are gospel-centered, seeing their primary earthly vocation as fostering their children's relationship with God. There is no guarantee that parental faithfulness will translate into faith for each and every child. Ultimately, genuine faith is the work of God in the heart of each and every person. Nevertheless, a vision of parenting should foundationally be one that cultivates faith and obedience—the fear of God which leads to heeding God's commanding word.

But faith does more than merely enable obedience. Faith in God fosters attachment to God. Entrusting oneself to God initiates us into a covenant relationship with God. Our relationship with the Lord is secure, guarded and protected by God's good promises and faithful character. As we experience intimacy and security in our relationship with the Lord, so we are able to cultivate a home environment that fosters healthy forms of bonding, attachment, and connection. <Callout>It is in the home where children first learn what healthy relationships entail.</Callout> By keeping God's covenant front and center in our home, we can even hope for faith formation in the generations to come.

###### Conclusion

Christian homebuilding is a matter of cultivating vibrant worship of the Lord, encountering God's tender love, experiencing God's compassionate care, and enjoying God's covenant faithfulness. Cultivating Christian hearth and home is a matter of receiving God's grace and mercy in our lives. Our homes and hearts become welcoming and hospitable to others once we experience the extraordinary and unparalleled divine welcome of God's forgiveness, mercy, and grace. When parents maintain a life and faith of vibrant worship, their homebuilding endeavors benefit from God's blessing. Ultimately, this is the main aim of all parenting work: loving our children toward the love of God. As parents, may our devotion to God build a home that is under God's benevolent rule. May our experience of God's love and goodness fuel us to love our children with compassion, mercy, and faithfulness. May we build a home that experiences God's righteous care for generations to come, even to our children's children!

##### Session Summary

- God is the ultimate example of parental love and care. We learn best about parenting from the way God loves and cares for his people.
- Our relationship with God as Father shapes our own parenting work. We can only give to our children what we receive from God.
- Christian parents are like priests, nurturing their family in the worship of God. A heart of devotion to God is fostered by habits and practices of regular family worship.
- Godly parenting seeks to place their home under God's covenant love, fully submitted to God's righteous rule. Christian homebuilding cultivates devotion to God: genuine faith that leads to covenantal obedience.
- To be in covenant relationship with God is to experience an attachment to God. Parents should develop healthy attachments and bonds with their children to help them learn what it is to enjoy an intimate and close relationship with God.
- The Christian home is a place to teach gospel truths: redemption, mercy, forgiveness, and grace. Ultimately, the parent-child relationship is to introduce children to relationship with God—not to maximize earthly life's temporary and fleeting pleasures, but find coverage in God's everlasting love.

#### Charting the Path Ahead

*Reflect on the session and envision next steps. Record key takeaways from the lesson. Conclude your time by praying as small groups and a whole community. Review next steps.*

##### Corporate Prayer

Bless the Lord, O my soul. Bless your holy name. Our Father in heaven, we cannot number the kind benefits you have shown to us. You have been to us a loving and tender Father. Help us to love our children as you have loved us. Grant us the power to teach them the fear of God. Make our home a place of worship and devotion to the Lord. Help us to celebrate you, to praise you, and to magnify you. Place our home under your covenant protection. Bring all of our children—each and every one—into a saving relationship with you. May they taste the goodness of God in their own hearts. Not in our strength, but by your power, help us to fulfill our calling as priests in our home. Keep us from the allure of temporary pleasures. Establish our family in the everlasting love of God. Guard us from stubborn resistance to your command. Assist us to find your righteous rule our sweet freedom and joy. Help us, O God! Amen!

- Meet with a mentor to review this session.
- Memorize the biblical proverb.
- Complete the spiritual disciplines over the course of the week.
- Finish your personal and parenting project.

Behold what manner of love the Father has given to us, that we should be called children of God. And that is what we are! The reason the world does not know us is that it did not know Him. Beloved, we are now children of God, and what we will be has not yet been revealed. We know that when Christ appears, we will be like Him, for we will see Him as He is.

**James 1:16–18**

Every good and perfect gift is from above, coming down from the Father of the heavenly lights, with whom there is no change or shifting shadow. He chose to give us birth through the word of truth, that we would be a kind of firstfruits of His creation.

#### Spiritual Practice

*Use the following activity as a concrete way to commune with the Lord. Set aside enough time to complete this activity in its entirety, following each step as a guide.*

##### Getting Quiet Before God

*Read the following verse out loud. Then, spend several minutes in silence before the Lord, acknowledging his presence.*

> But now, O Lord, You are our Father; we are the clay, and You are the potter; we are all the work of Your hand.

<< Isaiah 64:8

##### Acknowledging God as Father

*After several minutes of silence, offer this prayer to God. Pray with open hands facing upwards to symbolize you stand before God in complete openness.*

> Almighty God, I am weak and frail. Surely, I am a noble creation of your powerful hands. But I am also a fragile creature. My strength is limited. I am prone to temptation. I easily wander from your paths. I still struggle with pain from the past and uncertainty about the future. But I know your "power is perfected in weakness" (2 Corinthians 12:9). Help me to live by the reality "that when I am weak, then I am strong" (2 Corinthians 12:10). In your love and tender care, I am not overcome by enemies, not bound by sin, not plagued by the past, and not afraid of the days to come. Help me to rest in your covenant love and fatherly care. Amen.

##### Meditating on God's Tender Care

*If you can, find an object that is fragile (like a glass). Spend time staring at this object, reflecting on what makes it fragile and what kind of care is necessary*

When his spirit departs, he returns to the ground; on that very day his plans perish. Blessed is he whose help is the God of Jacob, whose hope is in the Lord his God, the Maker of heaven and earth, the sea, and everything in them. He remains faithful forever. He executes justice for the oppressed and gives food to the hungry. The Lord sets the prisoners free, 8 the Lord opens the eyes of the blind, the Lord lifts those who are weighed down, the Lord loves the righteous. The Lord protects foreigners; He sustains the fatherless and the widow, but the ways of the wicked He frustrates. The Lord reigns forever, your God, O Zion, for all generations. Hallelujah!

### Session 1 Reflective Projects

#### Personal Project

*The following activity helps you internalize the biblical teaching and develop theological wisdom for parenting by grappling with the implications of the teaching in your own life.*

##### Project Explanation

Write (or record) a descriptive portrait that expresses God's fatherly relationship with you and his people. (i.e., prayer, poem, recording, prose description, drawing, dramatization, narrative, etc.)

##### Example Prayer

Father, You have adopted me into your family; I am an heir of the Most High; you love me enough to discipline me; you want my best and forgive my worst; comfort comes from your nearness and your presence; you know I am weak and you still want me; you delight in me with Your everlasting love. Although I do not merit your love, you pour it out in abundance. Although I was estranged from you in my sin, you brought me near and adopted me into your family. No force or power in all the world can separate me from your love. I belong to you. In fact, my belonging to you is more significant than any achievement, accolade, or accomplishment. You are not satisfied and pleased with me because of my performance. You uphold me by the righteousness of your Son. I daily find myself drawn to lesser loves while I know that you are the spring and fountain of all joy. You are not harsh with me, though you are fierce in your wrath. You know my weakness, and you have sent your son to condescend to my loneliness. No greater father is there than my maker and redeemer. This is to whom I belong. Amen.

#### Parenting Project

*The role of a parent is to cultivate a home that worships God. We can nurture devotion to God as we practice faithful habits of family worship. Below is your opportunity to come up with a plan for family worship.*

##### Discuss with Your Spouse

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesOne-Ses1RefPro-ParPro-DisSpo-1">- **Discussing Core Values**: What key practices do you want to be in place as you and your family worship God together?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesOne-Ses1RefPro-ParPro-DisSpo-2">- **Anticipating the Future**: What are some of your greatest concerns about worshiping together as a family? What most excites you?</Question>

##### Project Explanation

###### Weekly Habits for Family Worship

In this project, you and your spouse should sketch out a typical week for your family. Identify the weekly rhythms that will help your family become a home of worship and devotion to the Lord. Consider fixed times for family dinner, family worship, and family recreation. Identify the specific habits and practices you want to incorporate in your family, considering the uniqueness of the morning, afternoon, and evening hours. Factor into your plan times of collective family worship, private devotion, and regular church fellowship.

List of basic spiritual habits:

- Bible Reading and Memorization
- Prayer and Fasting
- Sabbath Rest and Church Fellowship
- Service and Evangelism
- Generosity and Giving
- Praise and Worship

###### Family Worship Liturgy

Design a family worship session that you can use to lead your house in a time of praising the Lord. Look through the basic elements of a time of worship and seek to incorporate them into a liturgy—a planned and ordered time of worship. Consider how to make this time interactive with the members of your family, encouraging as much participation as possible.

List of basic elements of family worship:

- Scripture Reading
- Memorization
- Singing
- Prayer (Thanks, Praise, Confession, Petition)
- Catechism/Confession
- Encouragement

## Session Two

#### Between the Ages: Nurturing Faith in the Next Generation

##### Overview

> Then we Your people, the sheep of Your pasture, will thank You forever; from generation to generation we will declare Your praise.

<< Psalm 79:13

> The power for good or evil that resides in a little child is great beyond all human calculation. A child rightly trained may be a world-wide blessing, with an influence reaching onward to eternal years. But a neglected or misdirected child may live to blight and blast mankind, and leave influences of evil which shall roll on in increasing volume till they plunge into the gulf of eternal perdition.

<< George Müller, *George Müller of Bristol*

God is accomplishing his work throughout the ages. In every generation, God has preserved his people. Across the epochs of human history, God works his mighty salvation. The story of the world is the grand narrative of God achieving merciful rescue and gracious redemption of people from all cultures and all times. One of the main vehicles that passes the faith from one generation to the next is the family. Godly homes are tributaries that nurture and nourish devotion to God in the lives of others. Good or bad, the influence of a family extends for generations. By nature, families are intergenerational. Children, adults, and the elderly coexist in mutually edifying ways. But the intergenerational dynamic of the family precedes the current generation (through the influence of one's ancestors) and extends to those yet born (marking the lives of one's descendants). Importantly, the church—as a family of faith—is also an intergenerational community. Each generation must look back to its forefathers with thanksgiving and caution as it consider what it means to live out the faith in the present age. When children are born, our focus should (rightly) turn toward the future, reflecting how our parental work can pass on the faith for generations to come. Such is the great and noble work of parenting: stewards dutifully passing on the faith of our fathers.

##### Key Idea

As stewards, we will pass on the faith of our fathers.

### Session 2 Community Study

#### Tuning Our Hearts to the Lord

*Unite your hearts together in worship. Use the community confession, corporate song, Scripture reading, responsive call, and opening prayer to enter God's presence together.*

##### Community Confession

By God's grace and through faith in Christ, our home belongs to the Lord. As priests, we will nurture our children in God's fatherly care. **As stewards, we will pass on the faith of our fathers.** As shepherds, we will lead our children as God shepherds us. As teachers, we will instruct our household in the fear of the Lord. As protectors, we will entrust our family to the God's safekeeping. As overseers, we will build Christian hearth and home as a heritage from the Lord. As for me and my house, we will serve the Lord. For God's glory, for our good, and for the sake of the world! Amen and amen!

##### Corporate Song

###### Let Children Hear the Mighty Deeds

**Verse 1**
Let children hear the mighty deeds Which God performed of old, Which in our younger years we saw, And which our fathers told.

**Verse 2**
He bids us make his glories known, His works of power and grace; And we'll convey his wonders down Through every rising race.

**Verse 3**
Our lips shall tell them to our sons, And they again to theirs; That generations yet unborn May teach them to their heirs.

**Verse 4**
Thus shall they learn in God alone Their hope securely stands; That they may ne'er forget his works, But practise his commands.

##### Scripture Reading

He who has clean hands and a pure heart, who does not lift up his soul to an idol e or swear deceitfully. He will receive blessing from the Lord and vindication from the God of his salvation. Such is the generation of those who seek Him, who seek Your face, O God of Jacob.

<< Psalm 24:4–6

##### Responsive Call

**Reader**: Lord, You have been our dwelling place through all generations. Before the mountains were born or You brought forth the earth and the world, from everlasting to everlasting You are God.

**All**: I will sing of the loving devotion of the Lord forever; with my mouth I will proclaim Your faithfulness to all generations.

**Reader**: The words of the Lord are flawless, like silver refined in a furnace, like gold purified sevenfold. You, O Lord, will keep us; You will forever guard us from this generation.

**All**: For the Lord is good, and His loving devotion endures forever; His faithfulness continues to all generations.

<< Psalm 90:1–2; 89:1; 12:6–7; 100:5

##### Opening Prayer

God of the Ages, you have been faithful to your people in all generations. We confess: the word of the Lord endures forever. We proclaim: your works are mighty and merciful from age to age. We stand in between the generations to bear witness to your great name and your glorious redemption. We are beneficiaries, heirs of the faith from devoted generations that have come before. We are stewards, tasked with responsibly pass on the faith to the next generation. Help us to declare your word and works to our children. Assist us to make known your wonders our children's children. Empower us to build a Christian home to serves the generations yet born. Make us vehicles that keep the faith intact, preserve the truth, and recount your spectacular deeds. Form and fashion our home that every family member would learn to put their trust in God. Amen.

#### Seeking God’s Wisdom

*Focus your thinking around the key idea and biblical wisdom. Review the introduction and discuss the scriptural proverb to help orient you to the main theme of this session.*

##### Introduction

> Hear this, O elders; and give ear, all who dwell in the land. Has anything like this ever happened in your days or in the days of your fathers? Tell it to your children; let your children tell it to their children, and their children to the next generation.

<< Joel 1:2–3

> The Christian home is a stewardship. The parents are stewards of God .... They are invested only with delegated authority. Their home is held by them only in trust. It belongs to them in the same sense in which a household belongs to a steward. It is not at their absolute disposal .... These children are the heritage of the Lord; they are not at the absolute disposal of their parents; but merely entrusted to their care to be educated and dealt with according to the will of God .... Thus the interest of the child should be the reward of the parent. God will, it is true, reward the faithful steward of the family .... As the faithful stewards of God, we should dedicate our household in all respects to Him, and make it tributary to His glory.

<< Samuel Phillips, *The Christian Home*

God calls parents to be primary caretakers of their children. As caretakers, parents must assume the role of a faithful steward—a servant who seeks to use their position, power, and influence to diligently oversee that which has been entrusted to their care. God has not only entrusted our children to us, but he also charged us with the responsibility of delivering the truth to our children. Fundamentally, the primary duty of stewards is to please the master, putting into order a household that ultimately belongs to God. As stewards, parents recognize God as the master of their home. As such, God's will serves as the charter for all family life. His authority operates as the governing rule of the household. His revealed truth is the creed and canon confessed. His revealed word is the blueprint and design for family order. God has delegated to parents the responsibility to raise their children in the truth and pass on the faith to the next generations. In this way, children belong more to the Lord than they belong to their parents. The stewardship of parenting vocation requires that fathers and mothers see themselves as a part of an intergenerational community of faith, nurturing devotion to God in a way that preserves and promotes the faith for future generations.

##### Biblical Wisdom

Grandchildren are the crown of the aged, and the glory of a son is his father.

<< Proverbs 17:6

###### Core Principle

Parenting takes place in the midst of the generations. We are recipients of the past and cultivators of the future. The intergenerational nature of the family (and the Christian faith) is a most precious gift. Within a home, it is considered a great blessing to see one's children's children. As the proverb says, "grandchildren are the crown of the aged." Godly parents who see their children raise children of their own recognize this as a Godgiven privilege not experienced by everyone. Grandchildren are honor, joy, and dignity to those advanced in years. As much as grandparents bask in the blessing of grandchildren, children find great honor and dignity in their parents. The proverb teaches that "the glory of a son is his father." Children find importance, worth, meaning, and significance from their parents. Instinctively, children look up to their parents as objects of affection, sources of security, and models of emulation. Godly families well-ordered after God's design enjoy the rich interaction, mutual dependence, and joyous celebration of the generations. When families dysfunction and decay, generations turn against each other to their dishonor and hurt. But godly parents foster the health of their home by relishing in the intergenerational nature of childrearing—past, present, and future.

###### Group Discussion

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-SeeGodWis-BibWis-GroDis-1">1. What was your family experience like across the generations? How did you think about your grandparents and parents? Did they bring you a sense of honor or shame?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-SeeGodWis-BibWis-GroDis-2">2. What excites you about parenting being an intergenerational work? How do you hope to parent in a way that seeks for an intergenerational impact?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-SeeGodWis-BibWis-RecThoBel-1">###### Record Your Thoughts Below</Question>

#### Exploring the Biblical Text

*Study God's word together. Read the passage. Annotate the text and record your reflections on the following page. Answer the discussion questions, using the biblical commentary to help. Then, discuss the passage as a community.*

##### Scriptural Passage

<sup>78:1</sup> Give ear, O my people, to my instruction; listen to the words of my mouth. <sup>2</sup> I will open my mouth in parables; I will utter things hidden from the beginning, <sup>3</sup> that we have heard and known and our fathers have relayed to us. <sup>4</sup> We will not hide them from their children, but will declare to the next generation the praises of the Lord and His might, and the wonders He has performed. <sup>5</sup> For He established a testimony in Jacob and appointed a law in Israel, which He commanded our fathers to teach to their children, <sup>6</sup> that the coming generation would know them—even children yet to be born— to arise and tell their own children <sup>7</sup> that they should put their confidence in God, not forgetting His works, but keeping His commandments. <sup>8</sup> Then they will not be like their fathers, a stubborn and rebellious generation, whose heart was not loyal, whose spirit was not faithful to God.

<sup>9</sup> The archers of Ephraim turned back on the day of battle. <sup>10</sup> They failed to keep God's covenant and refused to live by His law. <sup>11</sup> They forgot what He had done, the wonders He had shown them. <sup>12</sup> He worked wonders before their fathers in the land of Egypt, in the region of Zoan. <sup>13</sup> He split the sea and brought them through; He set the waters upright like a wall. <sup>14</sup> He led them with a cloud by day and with a light of fire all night. <sup>15</sup> He split the rocks in the wilderness and gave them drink as abundant as the seas. <sup>16</sup> He brought streams from the stone and made water flow down like rivers.

<sup>17</sup> But they continued to sin against Him, rebelling in the desert against the Most High. <sup>18</sup> They willfully tested God by demanding the food they craved. <sup>19</sup> They spoke against God, saying, "Can God really prepare a table in the wilderness? <sup>20</sup> When He struck the rock, water gushed out and torrents raged. But can He also give bread or supply His people with meat?"

<sup>21</sup> Therefore the Lord heard and was filled with wrath; so a fire was kindled against Jacob, and His anger flared against Israel, <sup>22</sup> because they did not believe God or rely on His salvation. <sup>23</sup> Yet He commanded the clouds above and opened the doors of the heavens. <sup>24</sup> He rained down manna for them to eat; He gave them grain from heaven. <sup>25</sup> Man ate the bread of angels; He sent them food in abundance. <sup>26</sup> He stirred the east wind from the heavens and drove the south wind by His might. <sup>27</sup> He rained meat on them like dust, and winged birds like the sand of the sea. <sup>28</sup> He felled them in the midst of their camp, all around their dwellings. <sup>29</sup> So they ate and were well filled, for He gave them what they craved. <sup>30</sup> Yet before they had filled their desire, with the food still in their mouths, <sup>31</sup> God's anger flared against them, and He put to death their strongest and subdued the young men of Israel.

<sup>32</sup> In spite of all this, they kept on sinning; despite His wonderful works, they did not believe. <sup>33</sup> So He ended their days in futility, and their years in sudden terror. <sup>34</sup> When He slew them, they would seek Him; they repented and searched for God. <sup>35</sup> And they remembered that God was their Rock, that God Most High was their Redeemer. <sup>36</sup> But they deceived Him with their mouths, and lied to Him with their tongues. <sup>37</sup> Their hearts were disloyal to Him, and they were unfaithful to His covenant. <sup>38</sup> And yet He was compassionate; He forgave their iniquity and did not destroy them. He often restrained His anger and did not unleash His full wrath. <sup>39</sup> He remembered that they were but flesh, a passing breeze that does not return.

<sup>40</sup> How often they disobeyed Him in the wilderness and grieved Him in the desert! <sup>41</sup> Again and again they tested God and provoked the Holy One of Israel. <sup>42</sup> They did not remember His power— the day He redeemed them from the adversary, <sup>43</sup> when He performed His signs in Egypt and His wonders in the fields of Zoan. <sup>44</sup> He turned their rivers to blood, and from their streams they could not drink. <sup>45</sup> He sent swarms of flies that devoured them, and frogs that devastated them. <sup>46</sup> He gave their crops to the grasshopper, the fruit of their labor to the locust. <sup>47</sup> He killed their vines with hailstones and their sycamore-figs with sleet. <sup>48</sup> He abandoned their cattle to the hail and their livestock to bolts of lightning. <sup>49</sup> He unleashed His fury against them, wrath, indignation, and calamity—a band of destroying angels. <sup>50</sup> He cleared a path for His anger; He did not spare them from death but delivered their lives to the plague. <sup>51</sup> He struck all the firstborn of Egypt, the virility in the tents of Ham. <sup>52</sup> He led out His people like sheep and guided them like a flock in the wilderness. <sup>53</sup> He led them safely, so they did not fear, but the sea engulfed their enemies.

<sup>54</sup> He brought them to His holy land, to the mountain His right hand had acquired. <sup>55</sup> He drove out nations before them and apportioned their inheritance; He settled the tribes of Israel in their tents. <sup>56</sup> But they tested and disobeyed God Most High, for they did not keep His decrees. <sup>57</sup> They turned back and were faithless like their fathers, twisted like a faulty bow. <sup>58</sup> They enraged Him with their high places and provoked His jealousy with their idols. <sup>59</sup> On hearing it, God was furious and rejected Israel completely. <sup>60</sup> He abandoned the tabernacle of Shiloh, the tent He had pitched among men. <sup>61</sup> He delivered His strength to captivity, and His splendor to the hand of the adversary. <sup>62</sup> He surrendered His people to the sword because He was enraged by His heritage. <sup>63</sup> Fire consumed His young men, and their maidens were left without wedding songs. <sup>64</sup> His priests fell by the sword, but their widows could not lament.

<sup>65</sup> Then the Lord awoke as from sleep, like a mighty warrior overcome by wine. <sup>66</sup> He beat back His foes; He put them to everlasting shame. <sup>67</sup> He rejected the tent of Joseph and refused the tribe of Ephraim. <sup>68</sup> But He chose the tribe of Judah, Mount Zion, which He loved. <sup>69</sup> He built His sanctuary like the heights, like the earth He has established forever. <sup>70</sup> He chose David His servant and took him from the sheepfolds; <sup>71</sup> from tending the ewes He brought him to be shepherd of His people Jacob, of Israel His inheritance. <sup>72</sup> So David shepherded them with integrity of heart and guided them with skillful hands.

<< Psalm 78:1–72

##### Discussion Questions

###### Searching the Text

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-1">1. **Stewards of Truth**: How does this psalm describe the truth? What is the core content of the truth? How does it describe the action of delivering and receiving the truth?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-2">2. **Generations**: How did God's ancient people think about previous and future generations?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-3">3. **Community**: In ancient Israel, what role did the faith community have in passing the faith to the next generations? How did this relate to the role of the family?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-4">4. **Devotion to God**: How does this biblical passage describe what devotion to God looks like? How does it describe lack of faith in and devotion to God?</Question>

###### Seeking the Truth

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-1">1. **Stewards of Truth**: Why is it important for Christian parents to view themselves as stewards of the truth? How is parenting a matter passing the faith to the next generations?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-2">2. **Generations**: How should we think about previous and future generations? What biblical principles in this text will help make our parenting intentionally intergenerational?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-3">3. **Community**: What is the role of the community in faith formation? How should the church and the family work together in passing the faith to the next generation?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-4">4. **Devotion to God**: How can we tell when the faith has been passed on the to next generation? What should be the overarching goal parents have for their children?</Question>

###### Evaluating Our Lives

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-1">1. **Stewards of Truth**: How was the faith passed on to you (or not) from previous generations? Were there any believers in your ancestry that were instrumental in bringing the faith to your family?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-2">2. **Generations**: As you think about the previous generations (and your own parents) what are you grateful for? What do you want to reject?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-3">3. **Community**: How will you make your parenting intergenerational and community-based?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-4">4. **Devotion to God**: How will your parenting nurture devotion to God? How would you evaluate your confidence in God? How do you need to grow in confidence of God in order to better parent your children?</Question>

##### Passing the Faith to the Next Generations

<< But You, O Lord, sit enthroned forever; Your renown endures to all generations.

<< Psalm 102:12

> Every father of a family should consider himself as charged with the souls of those whom he hopes to leave behind him, and as contributing to the future propagation of the truth, by every act of devotion performed in his house. Wherever he has a tent, God should have an altar.

<< James W. Alexander, *Thoughts on Family Worship*

###### Introduction

When we think about the nature of a family unit, we must marvel at God's creative genius. Through families we maintain a connection to the distant past and leave a legacy for the coming future. It is not uncommon for a family unit to have three or four generations living at the same time, experiencing this intergenerational reality is real time. The tight-knit bonds of intergenerational family relationships are powerful, shaping our values, beliefs, character, and worldview. Each individual person owes his existence to an extended ancestry of marriages and births that were ultimately out of his control. Families exist to bring other humans into the world that will eventually form families of their own. Only God knows how the impact our lives and families will make in the distant future. According to God's design, the family is a self-propagating organism—called to be fruitful, multiply, and fill the earth. The joy of marriage naturally gives way to the desire for children.

But marriage and family are meant for more than a mere procreation. Because our children embody the future, it matters what kind of people our children become. Children require nurture, care, and guidance. Left to themselves, children will be misshapen and malformed. <Callout>Parents are frontline workers in faith formation:</Callout> *nurturing devotion to God by passing the faith to the next generation*. Psalm 78:1–8 is a spectacular parenting psalm that captures this vision for parenting. While surrounding culture defies God's design for family, marriage, and parenting, it is incumbent upon Christian parents to restore God's vision for godly parenting: parents are stewards of God's timeless truth who pass on the faith of the fathers to their children by cultivating a family life of intergenerational relationship, Christian community, and devotion to God. One of the greatest ways to impact society is by faithfully attending to the raising of our children after God's design. Let's be attentive to how this psalm can help us understand parenting as most sacred duty before God, toward our children, and for the sake of the world.

###### Our Fathers Have Relayed to Us: Parents as Stewards of Divine Truth

God has appointed parents as stewards of the truth. Godly leadership in the home must involve depositing the content of the faith to their children. Psalm 78 draws attention to this crucial calling in the family and the faith community. God's people can only reach maturity if they establish their lives on divinely revealed truth. As God's revelation to mankind, the Bible contains "instruction" (78:1) to be heeded. Through the Holy Spirit, God's inspired word has been preserved by the "words" (78:1) of his faithful followers. Divine truth is not always easy to understand, but, when it is embraced with faith, God's words are like "parables" (78:2) that help elucidate the riddles and quandaries of life. These parables record the story of God's redemptive work in saving his people. The truth of God's word is an ancient and timeless truth, revealing "things hidden from the beginning" (78:2) that were previously concealed but have been progressively revealed over time. God's word not only contains "law" (78:5)—commanding us in the ways of life—but also bears "testimony" (78:5) to God—inviting us to put our faith and trust in the Lord. Ultimately, the truth of God's word bears witness to God: declaring "the praises of the Lord and His might" (78:4), celebrating "the wonders He has performed" (78:4), and recounting "His works" (78:7). <Callout>Parents are best caretakers of their children by being faithful custodians of the truth.</Callout>

Parents must not be mere defenders of the truth. They must faithfully deliver the truth to their children. It is important that parents and families have a vision and strategy for communicating God's truth to their children. Helpfully, Psalm 78 offers a mosaic of terms to describe the act of delivering the truth: "open mouth" (78:2), "utter" (78:2), "relayed" (78:3), "not hide" (78:4), "declare" (78:4), and "tell" (78:6). While the psalm addresses the responsibility of the teacher in faithfully delivering the truth, it also enjoins the recipients to humbly accept the truth: "give ear" (78:1), "listen" (78:1), "heard" (78:3), and "known" (78:3; cf. 78:6). Communication of the truth is a two-way street: faithful teachers who pass on the truth intact to the next generation and a younger generation that is humble, teachable, and receptive to accept the truth as divine revelation.

Christian parents are temporary caretakers of their children. God has lent children to us for a short time in order to raise them in the faith. While we will always enjoy a parental relationship with our children, this relationship will change over the years. The years when children live in our home are to be focused on faith formation. <Callout>The aim of parenting is to eventually release the next generation into the world, rooted in uncompromising godliness and fervent faith.</Callout> From a biblical standpoint, the stewardship of children involves being custodians of divine revelation. At its most basic level, Christian formation in the home is a matter of delivering and receiving: Christian parents bear responsibility to faithfully and earnestly deliver the truth their children, and children bear the responsibility to humbly and simply receive the truth in genuine faith.

Like church leaders, parents are spiritual leaders in their home. One of the most fundamental jobs of a "parent as pastor" in homebuilding is to communicate God's truth to the family. Biblical truth should be the canon by which all other truth claims are measured. The character of God should be the defining standard of what is good, right, and moral. The testimony of God's works should form the exuberant confession and collective memory of the household. The unchanging ancient truths of Scripture should be the sure guide to navigate ever modern complexity and conundrum. The redemptive storyline of Scripture should shape worldviews about the true story of the world. A home and hearth built on the truth—testimony about God's holy character, inestimable worth, and redemptive work—grows a family strong. Strong families make the community healthy. Healthy communities impact and influence surrounding society. Leading one's home in faith formation is one of the best ways to leave a mark in the world that lasts beyond one's limited life. faith.

###### To the Next Generation: Being Intentional about Intergenerationality

The work of faith formation is an intergenerational work. But as this psalm attests, the influence and impact of generations is multifaceted. In one sense, we are the recipients of the faith from the previous generation: the truth is that which "we have heard and known and our fathers have relayed to us" (78:3). As recipients of the faith, the current generation is responsible to deliver the faith to next generation: the truth we have received "we will not hide them from their children, but will declare to the next generation" (78:4). This responsibility is a moral and spiritual duty assigned from God: God "commanded our fathers to teach to their children" (78:5). Our intergenerational duty should not be onerous but hopeful. We should bear witness to God's word and works so that "the coming generation would know them" (78:6). Our vision of faith formation should include "even children yet to be born" (78:6). But the aim of faith formation is not simply to deposit the content of the faith, but the capacity for each generation to pass on the faith for themselves. Even more, this vision of international faith formation aims to impact the unborn generation so that they will "to arise and tell their own children" (78:6). But not everything from past generations is worthy of emulation. Inasmuch as we should receive the faithful testimony of truth passed down, we should also be warned by faithless examples from the past: to "not be like their fathers, a stubborn and rebellious generation" (78:8).

The life of faith is intrinsically intergenerational. So should parenting intentionally be. <Callout>The Christian family is the glad beneficiary of the faith from saints in prior generations.</Callout> Even if one cannot identify Christians in their own family tree, each believer is indebted to the interconnected chain of families and communities who preserved the faith from generation to generation. As a believer, faithful saints in the past are your heritage—your spiritual fathers and mothers—even if they are not in your immediate bloodline. As parents, we should strive to make our parenting as intergenerational a possible. We should celebrate the ancient faith, rehearse the lives of the saints of old, share testimony of God's past dealings with his people. We must warn about the mistakes of the past and forecast the challenges of the future. We must train our children to not only embrace the truth, but have the competency to pass on the truth to others. We must be ever cautious of the danger of forgetting God. We must build strong our collective memory: frequently retelling the true stories of God's dealings with his people. We must see children as a heritage from the Lord. In the raising of children, we are nurturing future adults, those who will have families of their own. We should reflect on how our parenting work can impact three, four, or five generations into the future.

And no parenting plan would ever be complete, without a concerted effort to incorporate the faith community as a mainstay in their family life and faith formation efforts.

He Established a Testimony:

###### Recentering the Role of the Faith Community

The transfer of truth to the next generation is a community venture. The appeal to faith formation in this psalm is clearly set within the covenant community—"give ear, O my people" (78:1). God established his revealed truth "in Jacob" and "in Israel" (78:5). Both of these phrases serve as references to the collective of God's people. Even the repeated household terms in this passage—fathers (78:3, 5, 8) and children (78:4–6)—depict the larger corporate body of God's people as a faith family investing in the homebuilding of each individual family unit. The household of faith has the building of healthy family units as one of its main tasks. Not only does the family play a vital role in intergenerational faith formation, but God's people function like a family, sharing in the work of passing the faith to the next generations.

<Callout>Christian hearth-building must be set within the context of the faith community.</Callout> While the sphere of the family is sacred and God-ordained, individual family units do not possess within themselves all that is needed for childrearing in the ways of God. Although each family should function like a "little church," it should not be a replacement for the church. Within the faith community, parents find plentiful resources for their parenting vocation: intentional mentoring, marital exemplars, spiritual oversight, biblical teaching, meaningful fellowship, personal accountability, corporate worship, moral development, doctrinal instruction, habit formation, selfless service, material aid, and missional purpose. None of this means the parents forgo their primary shepherding role and hand over the child raising responsibility to the community. Rather, it means that godly parenting earnestly fulfills its faith formation responsibility by setting its household firmly the life of Christian community. Christian community assists in the passing of the faith to the next generation. The faith community is a like a spiritual incubation chamber that nurtures families, marriages, and children to be spiritually mature.

###### That They Should Put Their Confidence in God: Nurturing Devotion to the Lord

<Callout>Faith formation in the home and in the faith community aims to nurture people in devotion to God.</Callout> This psalm makes explicit the purpose of our intergenerational and community-based parenting work: "that they should put their confidence in God, not forgetting His works, but keeping His commandments" (78:7). This purpose statement highlights a threefold goal for the next generation: genuine trust in God himself, vigilant memory of God's deeds, and faithful obedience to God's word. True devotion to God must involve receptivity of the truth and rejection of falsehood. The psalmist describes the goal of faith formation as forsaking the faithlessness of previous generations: to "not be like their fathers, a stubborn and rebellious generation, whose heart was not loyal, whose spirit was not faithful to God" (78:8). But avoiding falsehood and error is not enough. We need to nurture children who entrust themselves to God.

Christian homebuilding is a matter of nurturing Christ followers in devotion to God. When parents communicate God's word to their children, too often they merely seek a child's behavioral conformity to family rules. While respect of a parent's authority, order in the home, and obedience to God's commands are important, none of these represents the overarching goal of Christin parenting. Above all, Christian parents should seek for their children to put their confidence in God (cf. 78:7). <Callout>Genuine faith in God</Callout> will express itself in faith devotion. A parent ought to forgo all convenience, any ease, and every worldly benefit for their children to have wholehearted trust God. When this faith is born in the child, parents must nurture this faith: helping them to not forget God's works and to express their faith in obedience to God's commands.

###### Again and Again: Retelling the Sacred Story to Our Sons and Daughters

The rest of the psalm (78:9–72) narrates the true stories of God's dealings with his people. The author cyclically rehearses key portions of Israel's history, telling of God's marvelous works—"what He had done, the wonders He had shown them" (78:10). This record of God's dealings with his people across the generations recounts God's miraculous liberation from Egyptian slavery (78:12– 14, 42–53), God's supernatural provision during wilderness wanderings (78:15–16, 19–20, 23–31, 40–41), God's gracious enablement to take the promised land (78:54–55), and God's righteous anger (78:21–22, 31, 59) and just punishment (78:30, 33–34, 59–64) for his people's faithlessness. Broadly speaking, the history of Israel tells a narrative of faithlessness. Despite God's glorious works, God's people showed cowardice in battle (78:9), infidelity to the covenant (78:10, 57), disobedience to God's commands (78:10, 40, 56), forgetfulness of God's works (78:11, 42), brazen and perpetual sin (78:17, 32), rebellion against God (78:17), willful testing of God (78:18, 41, 56), inordinate craving (78:18, 29), doubt and unbelief (78:19, 22, 32), lack of reliance upon God (78:22), false repentance (78:37–38), grieving God (78:40), provoking God (78:41), and the vile practice of idolatry (78:57– 58). This heavy and harrowing list of faithlessness is the result when people do not place their confidence in God (78:7, 22). Generations can go awry without faith in God. But God remains faithful, calling his people out of sin and into genuine repentance (78:32–37), undeserved grace (7:38– 39), and divine victory (78:65–72). The psalm ends with the hope of God's promised Messiah coming to deliver his chosen people. God under the skillful hands and pure character of God's chosen deliverer (78:67–72).

<Callout>The redemptive story faithfully recorded in the Bible is the faith heritage of every believer.</Callout> While God's truth can be stated in propositions, much of the Bible is an unfolding narrative of God's gracious work to redeem his people. Not only should parents rehearse the story of their own particular family, but they are responsible to ground their children in the story of stories. God's word records the history of God's ancient people as our story. Those who place their faith in God become inheritors of God's work among his people. We should retell the true stories of God's dealings with his people, because it tells the true story of the world. The faithlessness of our fathers serve as a grave warning. The enduring truth must become our firm bedrock. The wondrous works must stir us to worship and praise. God's grace and forgiveness should encourage us to embrace a broken and contrite heart of genuine repentance. By retelling the story, we proactively build a faith memory in our homes that encourages confidence in God and hope in his redeeming grace.

On the lap of a mother civilizations have been laid, as she sings, teaches, and comforts her little ones. Culture is built by fathers instructing and teaching their children about God's wise word and wondrous works. Through fireside chats and long strolling walks, grandparents have forged societies by their storytelling of the days of old. Pastors, teachers, and elders have been world-builders, telling the next generation the things that have been since the beginning.

###### Conclusion

Few vocations are more challenging and rewarding than parenting. <Callout>When God forms a family, he invites us to cultivate a home.</Callout> Christian homebuilding requires us to properly and precisely view ourselves as custodians of truth—divine revelation of God's words and works that serve as the only sure foundation for meaningful existence and everlasting life. Establishing a home on the truth will require us to grapple with the intergenerational nature of parenting—grateful for past faith heritage, dutiful in forming the next generation, and hopeful for impact across many future generations. The intergenerational perspective of godly parenting helps us see the impor- tant role of the community of faith—an intergenerational context to incubate faithful followers of God. All this work aims at cultivating devotion to God. May God help us rise up and form the next generation in our homes and church communities with this grand, God-sized vision that can sustain us in the midst of daily responsibilities, encourage us when undergoing great difficulty, and embolden us to stand firm regardless of the uncertain challenges on the horizon for each generation.

##### Session Summary

- The goal of parenting is to pass the faith to the next generations: to faithfully deliver God's word and fervently recount his works to the next generation.
- Parenting is an intergenerational endeavor. We are influenced by the past generations. We should seek to parent to influence generations of those not yet born.
- Godly families help the church grow; healthy churches help families mature. The church is a family of families that seeks to establish homes in the faith.
- Godly parents nurture faith in God: to put their confidence in God and follow his commands.
- Passing the faith to the next generation involves sharing the history of God's saving work: a true story of redemption that culminates in the work of Christ on the cross.

##### Small Group Prayer

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2ComStu-ChaPatAhe-SmaGroPra-1">How can I pray for **other members** of my community?</Question>

##### Corporate Prayer

Eternal God, you have been the dwelling place of your people for all generations. God who is not bound by time, accomplish your purpose from age to age. God who is not limited by place, work your redemption in all creation. God who is not subject to shadows of change, fulfill your word in every generation. Make us godly stewards, who faithfully testify to your word and fervently recount your works. Keep our children from forgetting, ignoring, or dismissing your marvelous deeds. Move them to place their confidence in the one and only true God. With thanksgiving, make us grateful for the faith of previous generations. With humility, help us learn from the mistakes of the past. By your grace, help us to break cycles of sin and end strongholds of wickedness. With earnestness, help us to invest in our children as a most noble calling. We consecrate our children to you. We embrace our parenting role as custodians and caretakers of precious little ones who ultimately belong to you. Help us, O God! Amen!

<< Psalm 139:23–24

##### Rest in God's Presence

*After praying to the Lord, sit in silence for a few minutes. Rest in God's presence, recognizing his knowledge of and love for you. After a few minutes of silence, pray this prayer.*

> Show me Your ways, O Lord; teach me Your paths. Guide me in Your truth and teach me, for You are the God of my salvation; all day long I wait for You.

<< Psalm 25:4–5

#### Topical Study

*Study the key themes of this session by reading and reflecting on parallel passages collected below.*

##### Verse Collection

*Prayerfully read through the selected passages of Scripture, identifying important truths they teach. Mark verses that you find encouraging.*

**Genesis 18:18–19**

Abraham will surely become a great and powerful nation, and through him all the nations of the earth will be blessed. For I have chosen him, so that he will command his children and his household after him to keep the way of the Lord by doing what is right and just, in order that the Lord may bring upon Abraham what He has promised.

**Deuteronomy 4:9**

Only be on your guard and diligently watch yourselves, so that you do not forget the things your eyes have seen, and so that they do not slip from your heart as long as you live. Teach them to your children and grandchildren.

**Deuteronomy 6:20–23**

In the future, when your son asks, "What is the meaning of the decrees and statutes and ordinances that the Lord our God has commanded you?" then you are to tell him, "We were slaves of Pharaoh in Egypt, but the Lord brought us out of Egypt with a mighty hand. Before our eyes the Lord inflicted great and devastating signs and wonders on Egypt, on Pharaoh, and on all his household. But He brought us out from there to lead us in and give us the land that He had sworn to our fathers.

**Deuteronomy 32:7**

Remember the days of old; consider the years long past. Ask your father, and he will tell you, your elders, and they will inform you.

**Deuteronomy 32:45–47**

When Moses had finished reciting all these words to all Israel, he said to them, "Take to heart all these words I testify among you today, so that you may command your children to carefully follow all the words of this law.For they are not idle words to you, because they are your life, and by them you will live long in the land that you are crossing the Jordan to possess."

**Judges 2:10–11**

After that whole generation had also been gathered to their fathers, another generation rose up who did not know the Lord or the works that He had done for Israel. And the Israelites did evil in the sight of the Lord and served the Baals.

**Psalm 22:27–31**

All the ends of the earth will remember and turn to the Lord. All the families of the nations will bow down before Him. For dominion belongs to the Lord and He rules over the nations. All the rich of the earth will feast and worship; all who go down to the dust will kneel before Him—even those unable to preserve their lives. Posterity will serve Him; they will declare the Lord to a new generation. They will come and proclaim His righteousness to a people yet unborn—all that He has done.

**Psalm 44:1**

We have heard with our ears, O God; our fathers have told us the work You did in their days, in the days of old.

**Psalm 48:12–14**

March around Zion, encircle her, count her towers, consider her ramparts, tour her citadels, that you may tell the next generation. For this God is our God forever and ever; He will be our guide even till death.

**Psalm 71:17–19**

O God, You have taught me from my youth, and to this day I proclaim Your marvelous deeds. Even when I am old and gray, do not forsake me, O God, until I proclaim Your power to the next generation, Your might to all who are to come. Your righteousness reaches to the heavens, O God, You who have done great things. Who, O God, is like You?

**Psalm 102:18–21**

Let this be written for the generation to come, so that a people not yet created may praise the Lord. For He looked down from the heights of His sanctuary; the Lord gazed out from heaven to earth to hear a prisoner's groaning, to release those condemned to death, that they may proclaim the name of the Lord in Zion and praise Him in Jerusalem.

**Psalm 103:17–18**

But from everlasting to everlasting the loving devotion of the Lord extends to those who fear Him, and His righteousness to their children's children—to those who keep His covenant and remember to obey His precepts.

**Psalm 145:3–5**

Great is the Lord and greatly to be praised; His greatness is unsearchable. One generation will commend Your works to the next, and will proclaim Your mighty acts—the glorious splendor of Your majesty. And I will meditate on Your wondrous works.

 **Isaiah 38:19**

The living, only the living, can thank You, as I do today; fathers will tell their children about Your faithfulness.

**2 Timothy 3:14–17**

But as for you, continue in the things you have learned and firmly believed, since you know from whom you have learned them. From infancy you have known the Holy Scriptures, which are able to make you wise for salvation through faith in Christ Jesus. All Scripture is God-breathed and is useful for instruction, for conviction, for correction, and for training in righteousness, so that the man of God may be complete, fully equipped for every good work.

##### Getting Quiet Before God

*Read the following verse out loud. Then, spend several minutes in silence before the Lord, acknowledging his presence.*

> But now, O Lord, You are our Father; we are the clay, and You are the potter; we are all the work of Your hand.

<< Isaiah 64:8

##### Acknowledging God as Father

*After several minutes of silence, offer this prayer to God. Pray with open hands facing upwards to symbolize you stand before God in complete openness.*

> Almighty God, you know my end from my beginning. In your sovereignty, you placed me in my family of origins. By your grace, I am now having a family of my own. I recognize that my parents were not perfect. But I also acknowledge that I was not blameless either. Help me to accept my upbrining with gratitude, thankful for the ways you preserved me. Assist me to order my own family according to your will, humbly seeking to honor you in all things. In this journey of parenting, thanks be to you that you are my loving heavenly Father and the church is my faith family. Form and shape our family as you see fit. I submit myself and surrender my family to you. Amen!

### Session 2 Reflective Projects

#### Personal Project

*The following activity helps you internalize the biblical teaching and develop theological wisdom for parenting by grappling with the implications of the teaching in your own life.*

##### Project Instructions

Take time to reflect on your upbringing and family heritage. Consider dynamics that give reason for gratitude (i.e., things you appreciate about your upbringing), forgiveness (i.e., things that you need to forgive your parents for), and repentance (i.e., things you need to confess and for which you need to ask for forgiveness). Write a letter to your parents that expresses these thoughts to them. In this letter cast a vision of what you want your parenting to be to impact future generations—a vision for the generations.

##### Example Letter

Mom and Dad, I am grateful for your faithfulness to the Lord in raising us as children. You loved each other well as husband and wife and that gave us security and stability in the home. You opened your home to guests. You served the church with focus and attention. I am sorry that I made seasons of life more difficult than they ought to have been. My anxiety and emotional struggles controlled my behavior in a way that made things difficult for the family. I did not fully respect you all the time. Please forgive me. I know that you were not perfect. There were times when I wished some things were different. I forgive you of these things and own my own responsibility during this time. I commit the past, present, and future to the Lord. Your loving son.

##### Letter to Your Parents

#### Parenting Project

*The role of a parent is to cultivate a home that worships God. We can nurture devotion to God as we practice faithful habits of family worship. Below is your opportunity to come up with a plan for family worship.*

##### Discuss with Your Spouse

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2RefPro-ParPro-DisSpo-1">- **Reflecting on Your Past**: What traditions did you have growing? How did these traditions shape you? How was your upbringing different than your spouse?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2RefPro-ParPro-DisSpo-2">- **Discussing Core Values**: How will you tradition your children in the words and works of God? How will your traditions be Godcentered and faith-building and not just human-centered and nostalgic?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesTwo-Ses2RefPro-ParPro-DisSpo-3">- **Anticipating the Future**: What are some of your greatest concerns about viewing yourself as a steward of the truth? What excites you about this work? How can you better prepare yourself fo the work?</Question>

##### Project Explanation

###### Monthly and Yearly Habits for Family Tradition

In this project, you and your spouse will think through how you want to pass the faith to your children. Specifically, you will chart out an annual and monthly plan for the year that allows you to proactively build a family tradition. Of course, these traditions can adjust as your family grows. But make sure that these traditions help foster confidence in God. Consider: "What would we want to do on a monthly and annual basis that will build a home that is marked by confidence in God?" Or: "How can we proactively plan annual and monthly rhythms that will help pass on the faith for four to five generations from now?"

Consider the following ideas:

- Family Vacation and Field Trips
- Service and Mission Opportunities
- Festal Celebrations and Holidays (Holy Days)
- Community Events
- Hospitality and Welcoming
- House Cleaning, Family Ordering, and Calendar Planning
- Formative and Educational Opportunities
- Outdoor and Nature Experiences
- Sabbaticals and Times of Spiritual Retreat
- Annual Examen, Reflection, Renewal, and Resolutions

##### Monthly Planning Calendar

## Session Three

#### Over the Flock: Tending to Our Children Like Shepherds

##### Overview

> I will raise up shepherds over them who will tend them, and they will no longer be afraid or dismayed, nor will any go missing, declares the Lord.

<< Jeremiah 23:4

> Christian parents! See and accept your blessed calling; you are the shepherds of the Divine love to tend and feed the lambs. In His Church the Chief Shepherd has many shepherds to care for the flock, but none who can so care for the lambs as the parents. 'He makes Him families like a flock:' it is to parental love, inspired and sanctified by redeeming love, that Jesus looks for the building up of His Church ... 'Feed My lambs:' when this word is made the law of a parent's duty, what gentleness and love will it inspire, what heavenly hope, what faithful, watchful care, and what an unceasing life of faith in the love and grace and blessing of Jesus on our home.

<< Andrew Murray, *The Children for Christ*

God has appointed parents over their children. But we must not wield parental authority merely for our own benefit, treating children like servants and slaves. Instead, we should be over our children like a good shepherd is over his beloved sheep. Christian parents are to view their home as God's flock entrusted to their care. There is great promise, inspiration, and practical help in viewing the parenting vocation as shepherding work. First, Christian parents are under-shepherds, caretakers who tend to their domestic flock as servants of the Good Shepherd, Jesus Christ. As such, Christian parents are sheep in God's flock before they are shepherds over their children. They learn to care for their children as they receive God's loving shepherding care. Second, shepherding work parallels duties of godly parents. Shepherds protect, guard, feed, and tend to the flock with utmost care. To embody the role of a shepherd in one's home is to display selfless love, put on Christlike humility, cultivate a watchful and vigilant spirit, and nourish their children in the love of God. As pastors tend the church as God's flock, Christian parents are to view their homes in a churchly fashion—as a flock that requires attentive and godly shepherding oversight.

##### Key Idea

As shepherds, we will lead our children as God shepherds us.

### Session 3 Community Study

#### Tuning Our Hearts to the Lord

*Unite your hearts together in worship. Use the community confession, corporate song, Scripture reading, responsive call, and opening prayer to enter God's presence together.*

##### Community Confession

By God's grace and through faith in Christ, our home belongs to the Lord. As priests, we will nurture our children in God's fatherly care. As stewards, we will pass on the faith of our fathers. **As shepherds, we will lead our children as God shepherds us.** As teachers, we will instruct our household in the fear of the Lord. As protectors, we will entrust our family to the God's safekeeping. As overseers, we will build Christian hearth and home as a heritage from the Lord. As for me and my house, we will serve the Lord. For God's glory, for our good, and for the sake of the world! Amen and amen!
