**Family Education Plan**

In this project, you will outline out an education plan for your children. You should think about various goals for each of your children across various spheres of life. Use the template on the following pages to describe goals and strategic plans for each child. Consider this plan an effort in instructing your children in the fear of the Lord.

- **Physical Objectives**: Goals for body, health, skills, and competencies.
- **Spiritual Objectives**: Goals for faith, character, and godly discernment.
- **Intellectual Objectives**: Goals for knowledge, understanding, and wisdom.
- **Relational Objectives**: Goals for relationships, friendships, and biblical community.
- **Learning Plan**: A concrete and measurable plan to achieve scripted goals.

## Session Five

#### Under God's Protection: Godly Discipline and Divine Protection

##### Overview

> For I am with you to save you, declares the Lord. Though I will completely destroy all the nations to which I have scattered you, I will not completely destroy you. Yet I will discipline you justly, and will by no means leave you unpunished.

<< Jeremiah 30:11

> The power for good or evil that resides in a little child is great beyond all human calculation. A child rightly trained may be a worldwide blessing, with an influence reaching onward to eternal years. But a neglected or misdirected child may live to blight and blast mankind, and leave influences of evil which shall roll on in increasing volume till they plunge into the gulf of eternal perdition."

<< George Müller, George Müller of Bristol

The world is a threatening place. Dangers abound. Enemies lurk. Opposition schemes. Trouble menaces. Life in this fallen world can often feel like fierce combat on a hazardous battlefield or an arduous journey in treacherous terrain. We face physical hardship, spiritual attack, emotional turmoil, and relational drama. While we feel this multifaceted peril in our own lives, we also recognize the surrounding danger as we press into our parenting work. To be entrusted with the care of children requires vigilance and attentiveness because of the dangerous surround in which we raise our children. Inherently, parenting a work of protection. Sin will tempt our children onto paths of destruction. Satan will launch attacks against our families. Opponents of Christianity will devalue biblical teaching. Surrounding culture will wage incessant war against the truths and values of the faith. In the midst of dangerous times and hazardous settings, parents are God's appointed protectors of their home. With watchful eye and faithfilled prudence, parents are tasked with defending, guarding, and protecting their home. But, as we will see, parents best fulfill this protector role as they learn to entrust themselves and their children into God's safekeeping.

##### Key Idea

As protectors, we will entrust our family to the God's safekeeping.

### Session 5 Community Study

#### Tuning Our Hearts to the Lord

*Unite your hearts together in worship. Use the community confession, corporate song, Scripture reading, responsive call, and opening prayer to enter God's presence together.*

##### Community Confession

By God's grace and through faith in Christ, our home belongs to the Lord. As priests, we will nurture our children in God's fatherly care. As stewards, we will pass on the faith of our fathers. As shepherds, we will lead our children as God shepherds us. As teachers, we will instruct our household in the fear of the Lord. **As protectors, we will entrust our family to the God's safekeeping.** As overseers, we will build Christian hearth and home as a heritage from the Lord. As for me and my house, we will serve the Lord. For God's glory, for our good, and for the sake of the world! Amen and amen!

##### Corporate Song

###### A Might Fortress Is Our God

**Verse 1**
A mighty fortress is our God, A bulwark never failing; Our helper he, amid the flood Of mortal ills prevailing. For still our ancient foe Does seek to work us woe; His craft and power are great, And armed with cruel hate, On earth is not his equal.

**Verse 2**
Did we in our own strength confide, our striving would be losing, were not the right Man on our side, the Man of God's own choosing. You ask who that may be? Christ Jesus, it is he; Lord Sabaoth his name, from age to age the same; and he must win the battle.

**Verse 3**
And though this world, with devils filled, Should threaten to undo us, We will not fear, for God has willed His truth to triumph through us. The prince of darkness grim, We tremble not for him; His rage we can endure, For lo! his doom is sure; One little word shall fell him.

**Verse 5**
That Word above all earthly powers No thanks to them abideth; The Spirit and the gifts are ours Through him who with us sideth. Let goods and kindred go, This mortal life also; The body they may kill: God's truth abideth still; His kingdom is forever!

##### Scripture Reading

He who dwells in the shelter of the Most High will abide in the shadow of the Almighty. I will say to the Lord, "You are my refuge and my fortress, my God, in whom I trust."

<< Psalm 91:1–2

##### Responsive Call

**Reader**: How can a young man keep his way pure? By guarding it according to Your word.

**All**: With all my heart I have sought You; do not let me stray from Your commandments.

**Reader**: I have hidden Your word in my heart that I might not sin against You.

**All**: Blessed are You, O Lord; teach me Your statutes.

<< Psalm 119:9–12

##### Opening Prayer

Almighty Lord, this world is filled with trouble, danger, and trial. But none of these threats is more powerful than you. You are our shelter from every peril. You are our refuge in the face of myriad danger. You are our fortress in the midst of all conflict. You are our security during battle, our safe-haven from temptation, and our conquering Lord against the spiritual foe. Your discipline is loving correction from the path of destruction. Your presence is our ever-present dwelling place. As we experience your all-powerful protection, help us to be protectors and guardians of our home. Make us vigilant, watchful, prudent, and circumspect. Help us to protect our children without pampering them, to oversee them without overindulging them. Ultimately, though, we entrust our home to your safekeeping. Watch over us and our children. Keep us from sin. Preserve us from trouble. Sustain us in difficulty. Save us from eternal condemnation and infernal judgment. Yes. Lord! Carry us to life everlasting. Amen!

#### Seeking God's Wisdom

*Focus your thinking around the key idea and biblical wisdom. Review the introduction and discuss the scriptural proverb to help orient you to the main theme of this session.*

##### Introduction

> Thus says the Lord your Redeemer, the Holy One of Israel: "I am the Lord your God, who teaches you for your benefit, who directs you in the way you should go. If only you had paid attention to My commandments, your peace would have been like a river, and your righteousness like waves of the sea.

<< Isaiah 48:17–18

> Precious, no doubt, are these little ones in your eyes; but if you love them, think often of their souls. No interest should weigh with you so much as their eternal interests. No part of them should be so dear to you as that part which will never die. The world, with all its glory, shall pass away; the hills shall melt; the heavens shall be wrapped together as a scroll; the sun shall cease to shine. But the spirit which dwells in those little creatures, whom you love so well, shall outlive them all .... Soul love is the soul of all love. To pet and pamper and indulge your child, as if this world was all he had to look to, and this life the only season for happiness—to do this is not true love, but cruelty. It is treating him like some beast of the earth, which has but one world to look to, and nothing after death. It is hiding from him that grand truth, which he ought to be made to learn from his very infancy,— that the chief end of his life is the salvation of his soul.

<< J. C. Ryle, The Duties of Parents

Love motivates and energizes parents to be protectors of their children. Like watchmen who guard a city, fathers and mothers are spiritual wardens of their home, protecting their children (and all who enter therein) from danger and threat. As parents, we know that we do not have the strength or wisdom to provide perfect security. This is why the parents first and best act is to entrust their home—themselves, their children, their guests—to God's safekeeping. Under God's watchful eye, a Christian home can become impregnable and unassailable. This does not mean that Christian families are immune to difficulty, pain, or hardship. On the contrary, some Christian homes may experience the greatest attacks and fiercest opponents. Nevertheless, a home under God's protection is most secure, and God will bring each of his children to ultimate safety. Godly discipline is part of a parent's protective work. Parental instruction aims to set children on the paths of life. Parental correction seeks to redirect children off of the paths of destruction. A home under God's protective care takes seriously its duty to raise children in the discipline and instruction of the Lord.

##### Biblical Wisdom

Discipline your son, for in that there is hope; do not be party to his death.

<< Proverbs 19:18

###### Core Principle

Parents are spiritual sentries—guarding their homes by keeping it under God's protective care. Parental discipline is one of the practical ways that parents can establish their home in God's safekeeping. This proverb tells us, "discipline your son, for in that there is hope." For parent and child, discipline can feel inconvenient, uncomfortable, painful, and intrusive. But godly discipline is a sign of genuine love. Biblical discipline sets the child on the path of life. In doing so, parents will "not be party to his death." When we forsake discipline, we make our home porous, allowing any number of danger and sin to enter the home, prey on our children, influence their minds, and subjugate their hearts. In essence, to forsake discipline is to be culpable of our children's destruction. It amounts to leaving door and window ajar, allowing any predator or threat to enter. But we need not be overwhelmed nor overcome by deadly dangers and snares in the world. We have a parental "hope" that gives peace, comfort, and consolation. Entrust your home to the Lord through the practice of godly discipline and make your home a fortress, a refuge, a citadel unto the Lord.

###### Group Discussion

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-SeeGodWis-BibWis-GroDis-1">1. What kind of discipline did you receive as a child? Would you describe this discipline as punitive, passive, or protective?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-SeeGodWis-BibWis-GroDis-2">2. What would change in your parenting if you viewed your role as a protector of your home? How would this change your approach to discipline, instruction, and correction?</Question>

###### Record Your Thoughts Below

#### Exploring the Biblical Text

*Study God's word together. Read the passage. Annotate the text and record your reflections on the following page. Answer the discussion questions, using the biblical commentary to help. Then, discuss the passage as a community.*

##### Scriptural Passage

<sup>94:1</sup> O Lord, God of vengeance, O God of vengeance, shine forth. <sup>2</sup> Rise up, O Judge of the earth; render a reward to the proud. <sup>3</sup> How long will the wicked, O Lord, how long will the wicked exult? <sup>4</sup> They pour out arrogant words; all workers of iniquity boast. <sup>5</sup> They crush Your people, O Lord; they oppress Your heritage. <sup>6</sup> They kill the widow and the foreigner; they murder the fatherless. <sup>7</sup> They say, "The Lord does not see; the God of Jacob pays no heed."

<sup>8</sup> Take notice, O senseless among the people! O fools, when will you be wise? <sup>9</sup> He who affixed the ear, can He not hear? He who formed the eye, can He not see? <sup>10</sup> He who admonishes the nations, does He not discipline? He who teaches man, does He lack knowledge? <sup>11</sup> The Lord knows the thoughts of man, that they are futile. <sup>12</sup> Blessed is the man You discipline, O Lord, and teach from Your law,

<sup>13</sup> to grant him relief from days of trouble, until a pit is dug for the wicked. <sup>14</sup> For the Lord will not forsake His people; He will never abandon His heritage. <sup>15</sup> Surely judgment will again be righteous, and all the upright in heart will follow it. <sup>16</sup> Who will rise up for me against the wicked? Who will stand for me against the workers of iniquity?

<sup>17</sup> Unless the Lord had been my helper, I would soon have dwelt in the abode of silence. <sup>18</sup> If I say, "My foot is slipping," Your loving devotion, O Lord, supports me. <sup>19</sup> When anxiety overwhelms me, Your consolation delights my soul. <sup>20</sup> Can a corrupt throne be Your ally—one devising mischief by decree? <sup>21</sup> They band together against the righteous and condemn the innocent to death. <sup>22</sup> But the Lord has been my stronghold, and my God is my rock of refuge. 23 He will bring upon them their own iniquity and destroy them for their wickedness. The Lord our God will destroy them.

<< Psalm 94:1–23

##### Discussion Questions

###### Searching the Text

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-1">1. **Surrounding Godlessness**: How does this psalm describe the evil days and evildoers? What does the psalmist ask God to do?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-2">2. **Godly Discipline**: How does God discipline his people? What is the character and aim of God's discipline?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-3">3. **Godly Protection**: How is God a protection for his people? What does God protect his people from?</Question>

###### Seeking the Truth

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-1">1. **Surrounding Godlessness**: What evil and wickedness oppose God and his people? Why is it important for parents to be aware of the evil days in which they are raising their children?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-2">2. **Godly Discipline**: What role should discipline have in raising our children? What is godly discipline, and how does godly discipline help create both wisdom and safety?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-3">3. **Godly Protection**: How should parents function as protectors of their home? How can parenting a matter of leading our families into God's protection?</Question>

###### Evaluating Our Lives

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-1">1. **Surrounding Godlessness**: What evil in the surrounding world most concerns you? What godless influences are you most worried will affect your family and children?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-2">2. **Godly Discipline**: What is your approach to godly discipline? How will you approach discipline in a way that God has disciplined us?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-3">3. **Godly Protection**: How have you aimed to make God your ultimate protection? How will you lead your family to rest in God's security and protection?</Question>

##### A Daring and Dangerous Venture

> I know, O Lord, that a man's way is not his own; no one who walks directs his own steps. Correct me, O Lord, but only with justice—not in Your anger, or You will bring me to nothing.

<< Jeremiah 10:23–24

> There is much more mercy in what seems to be harshness, than in false tenderness. Let the child see, that we are resolved; that we are not to be diverted from our duty by the cry of weakness or passion. Far better that the child should cry under healthful correction, than that the parent should afterwards cry under the bitter fruit to themselves and children, of neglected discipline ... Sharp chastening may fail later to accomplish, what a slight rebuke in the early course might have wrought. But is there not too often a voluntary blindness, that does not choose to see what it is painful to correct? The false notion—'Children will be children'—leads us often to pass over real faults, and consider their tempers and waywardness too trifling to require prompt correct. And thus sin, winked at in its beginnings, hardens in all strength of deep-rooted corruptions.

<< Charles Bridges, *Proverbs*

###### Introduction

The world is filled with danger—physical, spiritual, emotional, and relational. The broken and fractured systems of the world seem to multiply peril and hazard. Sin has corrupted God's good world and turned a garden paradise into a treacherous terrain. Daily, humanity experiences the world in dizzying conflict—evil opposing good, death taunting life, and wickedness seeking to undermine righteousness. In this world, it often seems like evil prevails, the wicked prosper, and enemies thrive. The world has rebelled against its Maker. Godless society is turned against the Lord. Culture is opposed to God. One should expect that, in a fallen world where sin rules as a cruel despot, those things which matter most to the Lord will be under attack. This is the case with the family. <Callout>In his revolt against the Lord, the prince of darkness marks the household as one of his most hated targets.</Callout>

However hostile is this world to the things of God, we need not (we should not!) lose hope. God is the refuge and fortress of his people living in a dangerous land. The church is a haven to the people of God. And, parents are God's appointed protectors over their homes. Psalm 94:1–23 gives us insight how to parent in evil days. This passage will help parents become vigilant in their homebuilding endeavor, raising godly children in a godless age. Helpfully, the psalmist highlights God's loving discipline through which he corrects and instructs his people toward wisdom. Those who heed God's discipline gain rest, security, and blessing. Importantly, God is the great example of all our parenting labors. <Callout>But God is more than just our parenting pattern. He is the safety and security to which all godly families run.</Callout> In the midst of a godless society and prevailing wickedness, building Christian hearth and home involves the work of placing our family in God's safekeeping. This passage that may not seem to offer immediate principles of parenting. But when it is studied on its own terms, we gain a theological vision—a Godcentered way of seeing the world and our parenting work—that serves as a great help in establishing our homes in the Lord.

###### How Long Will the Wicked Exult: Raising Godly Families in a Godless World

The psalm opens by calling out to God as the "God of vengeance" (94:1) and the "Judge of the earth" (94:2). This desperate plea to God is a petition for God to act: to "shine forth" (94:1), to "rise up" (94:2), and to "render a reward" (94:2). Essentially, it is a prayer for vindication: for God to dis- play his justice, act on behalf of his creation, and pay retribution to God's enemies. It is a confession that God's people live in evil times. Since the fall of Eden, God's people have always lived in a wicked world. Each generation of humanity can legitimately say, "The days are dark, the night is prolonged, and the age is perilous." The wicked prowl and the righteous suffer. The righteous psalmist asks for God to shine forth and dispel the darkness, to rise up and administer justice, and to pay back evildoers according to their corrupt ways.

As judge, God opposes those who oppose him. The objects of God's wrath are the "wicked" (94:3; cf. 94:13, 16, 20). The wicked are the "proud" (94:2) and "arrogant" (94:4) people who rejoice in evil (94:4), boast in wrongdoing (94:4), violate God's people (94:5), oppress the needy (94:6), and heedlessly reject God (94:7). They are "workers of iniquity" (94:4; cf. 94:16), who live contrary to God. Their godlessness is proven by their words (94:4, 7), heart intentions (94:2–3), and actions (94:5–6). The righteous psalmist asks God to no longer delay his judgment—"how long" (94:3)—but to act according to his holy and righteous character.

This psalm gives an honest picture of our sinful world. The days are evil.

The times are dangerous. The wicked menace and threaten. We live in a world opposed to God and antagonistic to God's people. Rebellion against God results in hostility to the community of faith. Faithful parenting takes place in dark and evil days. The world is opposed to God, expressing its rebellion in enmity, ill-will, and violence. Godly parents must reckon with the reality that evildoers abound and seek to supplant God's people—and their family—in their defiant rejection of God. Christian parents face many dangers in raising children in godless society. In an evil world, threat to the family can come in the form of physical danger, spiritual attack, mental suffering, emotional turmoil, moral compromise, and relational hardship. This many-sided attack to our homes compels us to develop vigilance and alertness. Few battlegrounds are more fierce than the warfare for our children.

While parenting requires a watchful spirit, it also demands a discerning eye. Some of the greatest threat and danger in our parenting comes from within the sinful human heart. Underneath all godlessness in society is pride (94:2–4)—the exaltation of self against God. all societal corruption comes from the sinful workings of the heart. Pride inevitably turns a person against God, God's people, and the needy (94:5–7). Pride is unprejudicial in who it attacks. In fact, it resides as a poison in every human heart—yes, even the hearts of our youngest children. The exaltation of self, is a subtle but sinister threat that endangers the home. <Callout>While parents raise their children in the midst of a godless society, they also do battle against he depraved and self-promoting human heart.</Callout>

The world is a dangerous place. God has appointed parents as protectors of their home, seeking refuge in God to establish his righteousness. Parents must guard their homes from wickedness and sin—resisting dangers from without and mortifying enemies from within. They must confront falsehood about God and cling to him in truth. They must abandon misplaced pleasure, rejoicing in that which dishonors God. Godly families must embrace a countercultural lifestyle and due diligence to dethrone the fiendish foe of pride. As we protect our homes by the shield of genuine godliness, our families can become protectors of others—to be defenders of the helpless and needy. <Callout>A godly home fosters a sense of justice in its collective consciousness such that it exerts the influence of its countercultural lifestyle on the surrounding world.</Callout> Ultimately, the godly home longs for God to establish justice on the earth. This is their enduring hope.

###### Blessed Is the Man You Discipline, O Lord: Committing to Discipline and Instruction

The second portion of this psalm addresses humanity. It calls people to "take notice" (94:8) and "be wise" (94:8). It is a summons for people to leave their senseless and foolish condition and to become wise and discerning (94:8). In this context, wisdom comes from a foundational truth: God knows all things. He created the ear and hears all (94:9). He made the eye and sees all (94:9). He "knows the thoughts of man, that they are futile" (94:11). God does not "lack knowledge" (94:10). Being all-knowing (omniscient), God instructs humanity: he admonishes, disciplines, and teaches (94:11; cf. 94:12). Contrary to a godless society, God's people are a new humanity in the fallen world. They live faithful to the Lord who sees all, knows all, and understands all. Living before God all-knowing and searching eye, God's people showcase to the world the manifold wisdom of God, a wisdom that comes from living under God's the authority of God's unerring word.

To heed God's instruction is to gain true wisdom, God-given understanding necessary to navigate this perilous world in which we live. Those who heed God's instruction receive God's favor: "blessed is the man You discipline, O Lord, and teach from Your law" (94:12). Those who heed God's word and submit to his discipline are granted "relief from days of trouble" (94:13). The wise and faithful instructed in God's word escape God's wrath, condemnation, and judgment which are reserved for the wicked.

There is a "pit ... dug for the wicked" (94:13), but the righteous will not fall into it. As God's people embrace a countercultural life—a life formed by discipline and instruction in God's word— God promises to "not forsake His people" and "never abandon His heritage" (94:14). God's righteous judgment will be estab- lished. God's justice becomes the code by which the godly live: "the upright in heart will follow it" (94:15).

Discipline and Instruction. Parenting amounts to raising children in the discipline and instruction of the Lord. Godly discipline involves both admonishment (rebuke, chastisement, correction) and teaching (instruction, formation, education). Like all Christian disciples, children need to know the paths of righteousness. They need to be taught and instructed. In the process of this instruction, beliefs and understanding find alignment with God's guiding word. But alignment to the truth can only happen if discipline counterbalances instruction. To know the paths of righteousness is different than walking in these paths. Discipline corrects and reorients children to God's ways when they stray from the path. As God models for us in this psalm, Christian parents must occupy the role of teacher: teaching and correcting, instructing and chastising, educating and rebuking.

Wisdom. To raise children in the discipline and instruction of the world is to cultivate a home of wisdom—calling children out of their senseless simplicity, youthful naiveté, and foolish ways into the ways of prudence and true understanding. The truly wise turn to God. In a godless society where people face the danger of proud evildoers and the pending reality of God's wrath, the safest place to be is among God's people. Wisdom teaches a person to heed these dangers and take refuge in God. God disciplines his people as a means to bring them into wisdom, to preserve them and bless them. The wise who take refuge in God—from godless society and divine wrath—love God's righteous correction and treasure God's eternal truth.

Countercultural Living. The wise who embrace God's word live a countercultural life. They are a contrast to godless society in the way they follow the paths of righteousness. <Callout>The Christian family is designed by God to incubate a countercultural lifestyle of biblical belief, godly living, and holy justice.</Callout> Family life should not only teach children how to navigate the dangers of a godless world; it should teach children how to live such a countercultural life such that they become a compelling witness to the world and a transforming influence on the world. Wise children formed in the family nest—formed by godly instruction and discipline become salt and light to dark and dangerous world.

###### The Lord Has Been My Stronghold: Seeking Divine Protection for Your Home

The psalmist celebrates God as protector. The wicked "band together against the righteous and condemn the innocent to death" (94:20). In the face of powerful systems of evil and wickedness, the righteous person recognizes their own weakness. At the foundation of their life and faith, God's people recognize their own frailty: their "foot is slipping" (94:18). They know that they pending death—"the abode of silence" (94:17). They are barraged by "anxiety [that] overwhelms" (94:19). All people are fragile in the face of human wickedness and divine wrath. But the righteous person finds safe haven in the Lord. He trusts God as his "helper" (94:17). He clings to God's "loving devotion" to support him (94:18). He rests in God's "consolation" (94:19) as a delight to his soul. For the righteous, God is a "stronghold" and "rock of refuge" (94:22). In fact, God is a conquering warrior who ultimately defeats the wicked. Speaking of the wicked, the psalm testifies that God brings "upon them their own iniquity" and destroys them "for their wickedness" (94:23). God is the one who rises up against the wicked and stands against the evildoers (94:16). God does not ally himself with the wicked (94:20). Instead, he is the guard and defense of his people.

In his power and faithfulness, God protects his people. <Callout>While parents need spiritual vigilance in order to rightly parent their children in a godless society, they also need childlike faith to entrust themselves to God's safekeeping.</Callout> The psalm that began in a plea for justice concludes with a confession of trust. The best thing a parent can do is the entrust its family to God's loving care. God will watch over, guard, and protect our children better than we can ever do. Parents best discharge their duty as protectors when they lead their home to trust God as stronghold and refuge. When God is our shelter and defense, we enjoy his loving devotion and fatherly comfort. To teach children how to find safety in God is foundational to all other parenting work. In fact, this rudimentary lesson is essential for our discipline plan to have godly effect. All godly correction and instruction is about making God our safety and security.

###### Conclusion

The battle for hearth and home is where spiritual combat is often most fierce. The enemy knows that if he can destroy the home, he can corrupt society, afflict the church, bruise the believer, revile the gospel, and oppose thew works of God. We all parent at a time when the days are evil. The fallen world presents a most challenging backdrop in which we must raise our children. But God is not surprised. Vigilant parents who seek for God's justice will submit themselves to God's disciplining hand. They will receive correction and instruction with humble faith. As God disciplines them, they will discipline their children—in love, patience, truth, and righteousness. Their discipline will be oriented to building wisdom and discernment. Further, parents will seek God as their ultimate security. They will lead their family by placing it under God's protective care. <Callout>Christian homes that are secure in God's stronghold can in turn become a safe haven for the needy and helpless around them.</Callout> Let's accept the challenge to raise our families with loving discipline so that they can be instruments of righteousness and justice in a evil and depraved world.

##### Session Summary

- We parent in evil days. The world is filled with danger and peril. Spiritual enemies seek to destroy families, attacking parents and children. Families face enemies from without (rebellious godless society) and within (proud sinful hearts)
- Godly discipline is an act of love toward our children. Godly discipline should be both instructive and corrective. Discipline is a way that parents act as protectors and guardians of their home.
- Godly discipline and instruction aims to cultivate wisdom and understanding. Biblical wisdom helps teaches children how to live skillfully in the world in a countercultural way that will be a witness of God's truth and a transforming influence in the world.
- Godly parents direct their children to trust in God. Parenting work involves cultivating faith in God's protective care: to not hide from God but to hide in God. Christian home are marked by God's protective care. Godly parents entrust their homes to God's safekeeping.

##### Small Group Prayer

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5ComStu-ChaPatAhe-SmaGroPra-1">How can I pray for **other members** of my community?</Question>

##### Corporate Prayer

Most High God, be our dwelling place. Help our home to make its home in you. As parents, we need you to be our refuge and fortress so that we can stand against foe and temptation, endure pain and suffering, and overcome weakness and frailty. Our greatest prayer is that you deliver our children—that you show them long life and satisfy them with your salvation. Grant to our family—each and every one life in your name. We surrender our hearth and home to you. As parents, we are your appointed watchmen over our children. Make us vigilant and aware. Keep us awake and alert. Grow us in grace and godliness. Help our discipline to be instructive and corrective, consistent and compassionate, formative and restorative, loving and just. May we teach our children—through word and example—not to hide from you, but how in faith to hide in you. Help us, O God! Amen!

> Search me, O God, and know my heart; test me and know my concerns. See if there is any offensive way in me; lead me in the way everlasting.

<< Psalm 139:23–24

> Show me Your ways, O Lord; teach me Your paths. Guide me in Your truth and teach me, for You are the God of my salvation; all day long I wait for You.

<< Psalm 25:4–5

*Study the key themes of this session by reading and reflecting on parallel passages collected below.*

##### Verse Collection

*Prayerfully read through the selected passages of Scripture, identifying important truths they teach. Mark verses that you find encouraging.*

**Deuteronomy 8:5–6**

So know in your heart that just as a man disciplines his son, so the Lord your God disciplines you. Therefore you shall keep the commandments of the Lord your God, walking in His ways and fearing Him.

**2 Samuel 7:11–15**

The Lord declares to you that He Himself will establish a house for you.And when your days are fulfilled and you rest with your fathers, I will raise up your descendant after you, who will come from your own body, and I will establish his kingdom. He will build a house for My Name, and I will establish the throne of his kingdom forever. I will be his Father, and he will be My son.b When he does wrong, I will discipline him with the rod of men and with the blows of the sons of men. But My loving devotion will never be removed from him as I removed it from Saul, whom I moved out of your way.

**Job 5:17**

Blessed indeed is the man whom God corrects; so do not despise the discipline of the Almighty.

**Psalm 118:15–18**

Shouts of joy and salvation resound in the tents of the righteous: "The right hand of the Lord performs with valor! The right hand of the Lord is exalted! The right hand of the Lord performs with valor!" I will not die, but I will live and proclaim what the Lord has done. The Lord disciplined me severely, but He has not given me over to death.

**Psalm 119:66–68**

Teach me good judgment and knowledge, for I believe in Your commandments. Before I was afflicted, I went astray; but now I keep Your word. You are good, and You do what is good; teach me Your statute.

**Proverbs 2:6–15**

For the Lord gives wisdom; from His mouth come knowledge and understanding. He stores up sound wisdom for the upright; He is a shield to those who walk with integrity, to guard the paths of justice and protect the way of His saints. Then you will discern righteousness and justice and equity—every good path. For wisdom will enter your heart, and knowledge will delight your soul. Discretion will watch over you, and understanding will guard you, to deliver you from the way of evil, from the man who speaks perversity, from those who leave the straight paths to walk in the ways of darkness, from those who enjoy doing evil and rejoice in the twistedness of evil, whose paths are crooked and whose ways are devious.

**Proverbs 3:11–12**

My son, do not reject the discipline of the Lord, and do not loathe His rebuke; for the Lord disciplines the one He loves, as does a father the son in whom he delights.

<< Proverbs 4:5–6

> Get wisdom, get understanding; do not forget my words or turn from them. Do not forsake wisdom, and she will preserve you; love her, and she will guard you.

**Proverbs 12:1**

Whoever loves discipline loves knowledge, but he who hates correction is stupid.

**Proverbs 13:24**

He who spares the rod hates his son, but he who loves him disciplines him diligently.

**Proverbs 14:26**

He who fears the Lord is secure in confidence, and his children shall have a place of refuge.

**Proverbs 17:10**

A rebuke cuts into a man of discernment deeper than a hundred lashes cut into a fool.

**Proverbs 22:15**

Foolishness is bound up in the heart of a child, but the rod of discipline drives it far from him

**Proverbs 23:13–14**

Do not withhold discipline from a child; although you strike him with a rod, he will not die. Strike him with a rod, and you will deliver his soul from Sheol.

**Luke 11:11–12**

What father among you, if his son asks for a fish, will give him a snake instead? Or if he asks for an egg, will give him a scorpion? So if you who are evil know how to give good gifts to your children, how much more will your Father in heaven give the Holy Spirit to those who ask Him!"

**1 Corinthians 11:31–32**

Now if we judged ourselves properly, we would not come under judgment. But when we are judged by the Lord, we are being disciplined so that we will not be condemned with the world.

**Colossians 3:20–21**

Children, obey your parents in everything, for this is pleasing to the Lord. Fathers, do not provoke your children, so they will not become discouraged.

**Revelation 3:19**

Those I love, I rebuke and discipline. Therefore be earnest and repent.

#### Spiritual Practice

*Use the following activity as a concrete way to commune with the Lord. Set aside enough time to complete this activity in its entirety, following each step as a guide.*

##### Getting Quiet Before God

*Read the following verse out loud. Then, spend several minutes in silence before the Lord, acknowledging his presence.*

> O Lord, they sought You in their distress; when You disciplined them, they poured out a quiet prayer.

<< Isaiah 26:16

##### Acknowledging God as Father

*After several minutes of silence, offer this prayer to God. Pray with open hands facing upwards to symbolize you stand before God in complete openness.*

> Gracious Lord, you are our refuge and fortress. We live in a world filled with danger and threat. No enemy can contend against you and succeed. For ourselves and our homes, we need your strength to be our protection. We need your discipline to correct our erring steps. We need your instruction guide us on the paths of righteousness. We need your understanding to give us wisdom. We need your faithfulness to be our shield and shelter. We entrust ourselves to you. Keep us under the shadow of your wings. May all your enemies see in us the beautiful wisdom of God put on display in our hearts, lives, speech, families, children. Amen.

##### Meditating on God's Tender Care

*Take 10 minutes to sit out in the sun, reflecting on the dangers, difficulties, and threats that you and your familiy face. Then, take 10 minutes under the shade to reflect on how God is your protection and refuge.*

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5WeeDis-SpiPra-MedGodTenCar-1">- These are dangers and threats that we face...</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5WeeDis-SpiPra-MedGodTenCar-2">- This is how God is our protection and refuge...</Question>

##### Praising God for His Care

*Come to God with humility and complete dependence. Ask him to cover the sins of the past and instruct you in the ways of his will for the future.*

> I lift up my eyes to the hills. From where does my help come? My help comes from the Lord, the Maker of heaven and earth. He will not allow your foot to slip; your Protector will not slumber. Behold, the Protector of Israel will neither slumber nor sleep. The Lord is your keeper; the Lord is the shade on your right hand. The sun will not strike you by day, nor the moon by night. The Lord will guard you from all evil; He will preserve your soul. The Lord will watch over your coming and going, both now and forevermore.

<< Psalm 121:1–8

##### Imaginging Life the Other Way

*Draw a circle on the ground. Imagine this space as fully protected by the Lord. Stand in the space and imagine how life would be if you entrusted yourself to the Lord's safekeeping.*

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5WeeDis-SpiPra-ImaLifOthWay-1">- This is how my life and family would look under God's safekeeping...</Question>

##### Entrusting Yourself to the Lord

*Entrust yourself to the Lord's care, offering him praise and honor as your caretaker, provider, and deliverer.*

> Therefore let all the godly pray to You while You may be found. Surely when great waters rise, they will not come near. You are my hiding place. You protect me from trouble; You surround me with songs of deliverance.

<< Psalm 32:6–7

### Session 5 Reflective Projects

#### Personal Project

*The following activity helps you internalize the biblical teaching and develop theological wisdom for parenting by grappling with the implications of the teaching in your own life.*

##### Project Instructions

Write a prayer of protection over you children. Use the language of Psalm 94:17–23 to guide your prayer. Put the names of your family members in the prayer.

##### Example Prayer

God, unless the Lord is Abigail's helper, she will dwell in silence. Her foot will be prone to slip, but may your loving devotion, compassion, and faithful care will support her. Help her to find security in your steadfast love. When she is anxious, be her consolation. When she is filled with sorrow, be the delight of her soul. While the evil prowl in the world, be Abigail's stronghold and rock of refuge. Do not let her form a foundation on shaking ground. Bring justice upon the wicked and establish Abigail in your loving grace.

##### Prayer of Protection

#### Parenting Project

*The role of a parent is to cultivate a home that worships God. We can nurture devotion to God as we practice faithful habits of family worship. Below is your opportunity to come up with a plan for family worship.*

##### Discuss with Your Spouse

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5RefPro-ParPro-DisSpo-1">- **Reflecting on Your Past**: What was discipline like in your upbringing? Looking back, what did you appreciate and not appreciate about this approach to discipline?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5RefPro-ParPro-DisSpo-2">- **Discussing Core Values**: What core principles do you want to guide your discipline of your children? How will you make your discipline both instructive and corrective?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesFiv-Ses5RefPro-ParPro-DisSpo-3">- **Anticipating the Future**: What are some of your greatest concerns about viewing yourself as a protector of your home? What excites you about this work? How can you better prepare yourself for the work?</Question>

##### Project Explanation

##### Family Discipline Plan

In this project, you and your spouse will outline a discipline plan for your family. You should consider the underlying convictions and principles that support your discipline goals as well as give concrete expressions to rules and strategies for raising your children in the faith. This should all result in a succinct family code that defines the discipline of the house.

- **Family Convictions**: The timeless, biblical truths that guide our house discipline.
- **Wisdom Principles**: The wisdom teachings that inform our approach to discipline.
- **House Rules**: The basic guidelines for conduct and family life that define and govern our home (general enough to apply to any circumstance).
- **Discipline Strategies**: The means by which you will restoratively correct and formatively instruct.
- **Family Code**: The rule of life or code of ethic that defines and orders your family life.

## Session Six

#### For the World: Leaving a Legacy in Society

##### Overview

> Then our sons will be like plants nurtured in their youth, our daughters like corner pillars carved to adorn a palace.

<< Psalm 144:12

> Youth is an ocean of dangers. Within, without, on every side they are beset with perils; the flesh is most strong and stirring, the world is most amiable and taking, besides, the wicked one is subtle and tempting, ever striving to hale them to hell ... Children are compared to arrows ... Now we know that sticks are not by nature arrows; they do not grow so, but they are made so; by nature they are knotty and ragged, but by art they are made smooth and handsome. So children by nature are rugged and untoward, but by education are refined and reformed, made pliable to the divine will and pleasure. They are also compared to corner-stones ... which are rough and unfit for use, as they are taken out of the quarry, and therefore must be hewn and carved before they are laid in the foundation.

<< George Swinnock, *The Christian Man's Calling*

Children are a gift from God. The sober responsibility of parenting children must be balanced with exuberant thanksgiving over the blessing of each child. Children bring joy to the present and represent a promise for the future. They signify God's favor and move us to deepened trust in God. They remind us of life's simplicity and press us into the profound. They make life full and offer a work that is fulfilling. They reflect us (in person, personality, and feature) but also urge us toward greater holiness of life and character. They receive the nurture from family only to eventually contribute to church, society, and world. God works out his purpose in the world through children. What we build on hearth and home—and what kind of children we launch into the world—leaves a lasting impact on the globe. In fact, to build Christian hearth and home according to God's design is one of the great ways to participate in God's mission in the world. This is one of the rich blessings of family life and children. Godly families raise children in the faith and send them out into the world as salt and light. Like arrows, children are shaped, sharpened, and sent into the world. Like stones, children are honed, carved, and established as part of God's people. With our families before us, we are servants of God, tending to our children as God's vessels. We build our homes to build God's kingdom. We sharpen our children to serve God's work in the world.

##### Key Idea

As overseers, we will build Christian hearth and home as a heritage from the Lord.

### Session 6 Community Study

#### Tuning Our Hearts to the Lord

*Unite your hearts together in worship. Use the community confession, corporate song, Scripture reading, responsive call, and opening prayer to enter God's presence together.*

##### Community Confession

By God's grace and through faith in Christ, our home belongs to the Lord. As priests, we will nurture our children in God's fatherly care. As stewards, we will pass on the faith of our fathers. As shepherds, we will lead our children as God shepherds us. As teachers, we will instruct our household in the fear of the Lord. As protectors, we will entrust our family to the God's safekeeping. **As overseers, we will build Christian hearth and home as a heritage from the Lord.** As for me and my house, we will serve the Lord. For God's glory, for our good, and for the sake of the world! Amen and amen!

##### Corporate Song

###### God Is Working This Purpose Out

**Verse 1**
1 God is working this purpose out, as year succeeds to year; God is working this purpose out, and the time is drawing near; nearer and nearer draws the time, the time that shall surely be: when the earth shall be filled with the glory of God as the waters cover the sea.

**Verse 2**
From utmost east to utmost west, where human feet have trod, by the mouth of many messengers goes forth the voice of God: "Give ear to me, ye continents, ye isles, give ear to me, that the earth may be filled with the glory of God as the waters cover the sea."

**Verse 3**
Let us go forth in the strength of God, with the banner of Christ unfurled, that the light of the glorious gospel of truth may shine throughout the world. Let us all fight with sorrow and sin to set the captives free, that the earth may be filled with the glory of God as the waters cover the sea.

**Verse 4**
All we can do is nothing worth unless God blesses the deed. Vainly we hope for the harvest-tide till God gives life to the seed. Yet nearer and nearer draws the time, the time that shall surely be, when the earth shall be filled with the glory of God as the waters cover the sea.

##### Scripture Reading

Now Moses was faithful as a servant in all God's house, testifying to what would be spoken later. But Christ is faithful as the Son over God's house. And we are His house, if we hold firmly to our confidence and the hope of which we boast.

<< Hebrews 3:5–6

##### Responsive Call

**All**: Come, bless the Lord, all you servants of the Lord who serve by night in the house of the Lord!

**Reader**: Lift up your hands to the sanctuary and bless the Lord.

**All**: May the Lord, the Maker of heaven and earth, bless you from Zion.

<< Psalm 134:1–3

##### Opening Prayer

Holy Lord, we receive our assignment as your humble servants. Ours is a home assignment: to build our family on the foundation of Christ. We know that this will be difficult and demanding work. Strengthen us for this noble task. We know that this work holds great promise. Comfort us when we fail. Console us when we grieve. Correct us when we err. Help our homebuilding work to be fully submitted to your will, oriented to your purpose, and supported by your grace. Our children are a heritage from God. The gift of our children we consecrate back to your care. Grant our children sincere faith in Christ. Teach them to keep in step with the Spirit. Make the glory of God their all-consuming passion. Unless the Lord build this kind of house, all of our efforts are in vain. Great Architect who has built the heavens, establish our hearth and home as one of your holy array. Assist us in this great work, we pray. Amen.

#### Seeking God's Wisdom

*Focus your thinking around the key idea and biblical wisdom. Review the introduction and discuss the scriptural proverb to help orient you to the main theme of this session.*

##### Introduction

> The bows of the mighty are broken, but the feeble are equipped with strength. The well-fed hire themselves out for food, but the starving hunger no more. The barren woman gives birth to seven, but she who has many sons pines away.

<< 1 Samuel 2:4–5

> Observe here, Children of the youth are arrows in the hand, which, with prudence, may be directed aright to the mark, God's glory and the service of their generation; but afterwards, when they have gone abroad into the world, they are arrows out of the hand; it is too late to bend them then. But these arrows in the hand too often prove arrows in the heart, a constant grief to their godly parents, whose gray hairs they bring with sorrow to the grave.

<< Matthew Henry, *Commentary*

God is working his purpose out. His will is guaranteed to come to fruition. He has an eternal plan to restore his fallen creation and redeem his people for himself. God is unhindered in this work. In his eternal plan, God will triumph over evil and vanquish all of his enemies, forgiving sinners, saving the lost, and restoring fallen creation to everlasting bliss. As we experience God's saving grace in our lives, he invites us to join his mission in the world. To accomplish his grand and glorious purpose, God sent his Son, Jesus Christ, into the world. Jesus is God's one and only Son, who accomplished for humanity a work that he alone could perform. Nevertheless, as believers in Christ, one way for us to participate in God's mission is for us to send our sons and daughters into the world ready to serve God, follow his Son, and do his will. This puts parenting work in the center of God's mission. As we experience the blessing of children, we should view Christian homebuilding as a way of participating in God's global work. In raising godly children, sharpening them as arrows and honing them like stones, we can change the world—for the gospel and for God's glory.

##### Biblical Wisdom

By wisdom a house is built and by understanding it is established; through knowledge its rooms are filled with every precious and beautiful treasure.

<< Proverbs 24:3–4

###### Core Principle

Parenting is homebuilding work. This proverb reminds us that we need prudence to build our homes after God's design: "by wisdom a house is built and by understanding it is established." In short, a strong, mature, and established home is rooted in biblical wisdom. Parents need wisdom to lay the foundation of a godly family. In addition, parents need to instill wisdom to their children. But parenting is more than just building a strong home. It aims for a flourishing family. The flourishing of the godly family is one of its great testimonies in the surrounding world. This proverbs tells us about a house built by wisdom: "through knowledge its rooms are filled with every precious and beautiful treasure." To build Christian hearth and home God's way is to experience the promise of divine favor in abundance. We not only need God's truth to understand the blueprint of a godly family; we also need God's strength to build our home in God's way..

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-SeeGodWis-BibWis-GroDis-2">2. What do you envision when you think about a thriving and flourishing home? What it look like for your home to be strong, established, precious, and beautiful?</Question>

#### Exploring the Biblical Text

##### Scriptural Passage

He will not be put to shame when he confronts the enemies at the gate.

<< Psalm 127:1–5

<sup>128:1</sup> Blessed are all who fear the Lord, who walk in His ways! <sup>2</sup> For when you eat the fruit of your labor, blessings and prosperity will be yours. <sup>3</sup> Your wife will be like a fruitful vine flourishing within your house, your sons like olive shoots sitting around your table. <sup>4</sup> In this way indeed shall blessing come to the man who fears the Lord. <sup>5</sup> May the Lord bless you from Zion, that you may see the prosperity of Jerusalem all the days of your life, <sup>6</sup> that you may see your children's children. Peace be upon Israel!

<< Psalm 128:1–6

##### Discussion Questions

###### Searching the Text

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-1">1. **Homebuilding**: What do these psalms have to say about homebuilding? How does a home get established in the Lord?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-2">2. **Devotion to God**: How do these passages describe devotion to God?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-3">3. **Blessings**: What blessings to godly families enjoy?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeaTex-4">4. **Impact**: How do these psalms describe the role of the family in God's work and purpose?</Question>

###### Seeking the Truth

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-1">1. **Homebuilding**: What is homebuilding? What is it meaningful work?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-SeeTru-2">2. **Devotion to God**: How can parents display their devotion to God in the way they parent and raise their children?</Question>

###### Evaluating Our Lives

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-1">1. **Homebuilding**: Do you view Christian homebuilding as meaningful work? What truths support this idea? What wrong ideas distort this perspective?</Question>

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-2">2. **Devotion to God**: Do you have an "unless the Lord" mentality? How well are you modeling devotion to God in the way you go about your parenting work?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-3">3. **Blessings**: How have you experienced God's blessing and favor in your home?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ExpBibTex-DisQue-EvaLiv-4">4. **Impact**: As you think about raising your kids to release them into the world, what most excites you about this prospect? What feels most challenging about this idea?</Question>

##### Of Arrows, Quivers, and Olive Shoots

> O house of Israel, bless the Lord; O house of Aaron, bless the Lord; O house of Levi, bless the Lord; you who fear the Lord, bless the Lord! Blessed be the Lord from Zion— He who dwells in Jerusalem. Hallelujah!

<< Psalm 135:19–21

> Every Christian family ought to be as it were a little church, consecrated to Christ, and wholly influenced and governed by his rules.

<< Jonathan Edwards, *Farewell Sermon*

###### Introduction

All families have a purpose. A family's values are shaped by this purpose, creating a sort of household culture. Misguided purposes and values can corrupt a family's life and do damage to a child's formation. But godly aims can sanctify and prune a family to be a sharpened tool in the hand of God. Recognizing that family's have a purpose is an important first step. A brief glance at a family' budget (how they spend their money), calendar (how they spend their time), and conversation (what they talk about) all serve as a barometers, revealing the overarching purpose of that household. Family habits and traditions also reveal and expose a family's mission. The guests we entertain and the friends we share life with also give us a clue into what our families are all about—their driving cause and reason for existence. Just like all humans live for something, all families operate their collective life by some underling purpose.

<Callout>In order to build Christian hearth and home in a godly way, we must be grounded in godly purpose and mission.</Callout> God has given us the blessing of family not to be hoarded and clutched for our own enjoyment. The gift of family life is only realized to its fullest as we enlist our families in God's global work in the world. The portrait of a pious home in Psalm 127:1–5 and 128:1–6 helps us understand what values, purposes, and aims should define family life. As we build Christian hearth and home, we must understand that God is building a house for himself. This is not a house of brick and mortar, wood and stone. He is building a house of his people. Amazingly, our homebuilding efforts can contribute to this great work of God in the world. Let us attend to these coupled psalms with open hearts, wise minds, and ready hands as we consider what it means to place our homes in the establishing, safekeeping, and benevolent hands of our trustworthy Lord.

###### Building the House: Viewing Homebuilding as Meaningful Work

Establishing a home is good and godly work. The opening of the psalm highlights and honors the work of building a house (127:1). In the Old Testament, the idea of a house can speak about a physical dwelling place, a family unit, an entire ancestry, and the temple (the dwelling place of God where he met with his people). In biblical thought and in the Christian life, these are all connected. Part of God's overall mission is to redeem and build a people for his name. The building of God's people takes place through godly family units that extend their faith influence across generations. The building of a godly house is intensely spiritual work: raising godly children, cultivating a Christ-centered home culture, fortifying God's covenant people, and influencing wider society.

In building a house God's way, we hope to experience a fruitful and flourishing home. The great fruitfulness of a thriving home is not food that we eat but the children we bear. In this portion of the Bible, children are compared to "olive shoots" who come from the "fruitful vine" of the blessed and pious wife (128:3). God's blessing expressed in the form of children is considered both "the fruit of the womb" and God's "reward" to his people (127:3). But the godly family exists for the prosperity of something beyond its own household unit. In Psalm 127:1, the building of the house is parallel with the protection of the city. Psalm 128:5–6 attests that the long life of the God-fearer is gifted with seeing "the prosperity of Jerusalem" and his "children's children." In these psalms the building of the family is parallel with the secure establishing of the city—the collective of families that form the community. <Callout>Building hearth and home is set within the larger endeavor of establishing God's people and securing the best for larger society.</Callout>

Importantly, the text points out the vanity of trying to do homebuilding in our own efforts. God alone makes our efforts meaningful and purposeful. This is not saying that human work is in vain. It says that human work without the Lord's undertaking is in vain. Builders still should "labor" (127:1) and watchmen should still "stand guard" (127:1). Diligent work may still cause us to "rise early and stay up late" (127:2). The difference is this: those who fear the Lord do not do their work in anxious toil. Those who give themselves to the Lord in wholehearted trust can enjoy God's provision and "eat the fruit of your labor" (128:2). The faithful know that the building of the home, the security of the city, the fruitfulness of one's work is dependent upon God's help and enablement.

While these psalms speak about a meaningful work in general—honoring the dignity of all good vocations—the biblical texts are extremely familycentric. Certainly, believers should seek good work: building, securing, watching, toiling, and making (127:1–2; 128:2). The labor of our hands matters to the Lord. In fact, God has prepared good work for his people. Our job is to walk in the work that God has prepared in advance for us. When we consider the full scope of our lifework—the total work of our lives that we offer to the Lord—one of the most signifiant things we can do is to build godly families. The psalms attest to that fact that healthy and holy families are a core element for all of the other work that we do. Godly families give work meaning, help work endure, and make work enjoyable. <Callout>Building a godly household is one of the main ways we can have influence in God's covenant people and in surrounding world.</Callout>

###### Unless the Lord: Establishing Deep Dependence upon the Lord

Both psalms invite families into a deep devotion to God. The repeated refrain "unless the Lord" (127:1) is a statement of faith as it is of fact. No household can be established, just like no city can be secured, unless the Lord does the work. God's people are marked by a wholehearted reliance upon God. This is more than external religious show. Genuine trust is an enduring quality because it is an internal reality. Utter dependence upon the Lord is born out of the fear of the Lord. Not only will God's blessing be upon "the man who fears the Lord" (128:4), but divine benevolence will extend to "all who fear the Lord" (128:1). Sincere faith expressed in the fear of God reforms our conduct so that we "walk in His ways" (128:1).

Better than decorating a home with material embellishments is to furnish a home with fear of the Lord—a husband who leads the home out of a vibrant personal faith in the Lord, a wife who is fruitful in home and faithful in devotion to God, and children who trust, love, worship, and obey God. <Callout>The personal faith of the individual members of a household make up the real collective character of a home.</Callout> Equally, individual expressions of faith are molded by the family's overall culture of God-fearing devotion to God. Exemplified by a godly father, modeled by a pious mother, and embraced by dutiful children, the fear of God underlies all other God-honoring family activity. If a family wants to be oriented to God, impactful in the world, and blessing for generations to come, it begins with this most important beginning of personal and household faith.

###### May the Lord Bless You: Enjoying Divine Favor, Full Peace, and True Prosperity

The fear of the Lord puts us in the path to receive God's blessing (127:5; 128:1–2, 4–5) and guards us from vain pursuits (127:1–2), anxious toil (127:2), shameful scorn (127:5), and hopeless need (128:2, 5). Those who entrust themselves to the Lord in wholehearted trust experience divinely given rest: "He gives sleep to His beloved" (127:2). God causes them to flourish (128:3) and extends to him his goodness: "blessings and prosperity will be yours" (128:2; cf. 128:5). Faithful God-fearers also enjoy God's promise of peace: "peace be upon Israel" (128:6). While God's people enjoy his blessings in all areas of life, God's blessings on are particularly experienced within the home: "your wife will be like a fruitful vine flourishing within your house, your sons like olive shoots sitting around your table" (128:3).

It is easy for families to get entangled in worldly pursuits. Surrounding culture endlessly allures people toward its broken version of the good life. Its great marketing strategy is pleasure, enjoyment, and happiness. But it cannot deliver on what it promises. The world's vision of the good life is a crooked path that will lead to destruction. One of its focused targets is families and children. Surrounded by ideologies of the world, parents can feel pressure to acquiesce to the world's version of the good life. Without thinking, families can embrace a pace of life, invest in a flurry of activities, spend an inordinate amount of money all in pursuit of worldly happiness. Parents can compare themselves with other families and measure their parenting worth by the earthly possessions and temporal experiences they give their children. But it is a fool's errand to chase elusive and disappointing delights of the world. Instead, we ought to seek God's blessing. A family devoted to the Lord can enjoy true prosperity: enduring peace, profound joy, sustained rest, and everlasting life. Godly families forsake the pursuit of worldly happiness to embrace the superior offer of divine blessing.

###### When He Confronts the Enemies: Treating Family Life as a Battlefront Combat

Psalm 127 concludes by saying that a full and flourishing home will be a man's honor and defense in the public sector: "he will not be put to shame when he confronts the enemies at the gate" (127:5). Because there is a moral, religious, and spiritual conflict that exists in this fallen world, the life of faith is depicted as warfare. In a society opposed to God, God's people must prepare themselves to face enemies and opposition. This psalm attests that godly families are one of the greatest weapons in the fight of the faith. Children are compared to "arrows in the hand of a warrior" (127:4). The man who is not ashamed is the man "whose quiver is full of them" (127:5). The man who has "children born in one's youth" (127:4) is depicted as a man of honor, vigor, and valor. While having many children is a true blessing from God, Psalms 127–128 put together refuse for us to turn our children into idols. A family dedicated to the Lord—along with children who fear God (cf. 128:1, 4)—are considered God's beloved (127:2). God is working through godly families for something bigger than the family. As arrows are meant to be launched into the world (and in particular, released in battle), a godly home raises children not only as a heritage but as a weapon for the Lord's work.

<Callout>A well-ordered home aligned after God's design is one of our greatest testimonies in and defenses against a godless society.</Callout> As Christians, we confront godless culture by building godly families. We invest in a hopeful future by raising Christian children. We battle against a lost society—expressed in moral deviance, false doctrine, gross injustice, errant ideology, and distorted worldview—by cultivating the fear of God in the home. We bring about transformation in the larger world by building Christian hearth and home. In our parenting work, we are not simply nurturing children, but raising adults, who embrace the faith and serve the Lord in their own generation. Importantly, the battle for society takes place on the mantle of the family. <Callout>The personal heritage and blessing that is a godly family is also a redemptive blessing and spiritual influence to our fallen world.</Callout>

###### May See Your Children's Children: Hoping for Generational Impact

Godly parents who take their responsibility seriously not only seek to raise children fit for the fight of faith, they also seek to make a generational impact. In God's design, families extend beyond the life of their parents. If taken seriously, parents can establish a home that transfers godly values, biblical ideals, pious examples, and timeless truth into the next generation. These biblical texts say that "children are indeed a heritage from the Lord" (127:3). In fact, godly parents are given a vision of seeing their "children's children" (128:6). The blessing of seeing faithful followers of God in subsequent generations outshines any prospect of material wealth, public renown, vocational advancement, bountiful fare, or palatial estate. These psalms summon us to invest in our children, considering how our parenting work can impact generations to come. Moreover, they call us to invest in that which lasts—forsaking treasures on earth to store up treasures in heaven. Parenting our children in a godly way can be (and should be) an investment in these heavenly treasures.

These psalms serve like wisdom sayings. They offer us a reliable portrait for how things work in God's economy, but their do not guarantee these realities for every single parental experience. Tragically, not every godly parent will meet their grandchildren. Sadly, not every godly family will bear children. Not every parent who fears the Lord will have children who follow the Lord. Many times, God's promised blessings may not materialize this side of eternity. Nevertheless, this does not mean God's promises are not true and trustworthy. Instead, the portrait of a pious home with God's promised blessings will certainly come to fruition in the world to come, if they do not come or only come in part in this life. Eventually, the generations will end, and the Lord will return. Only then, in retrospect, will we be able to see how our invest in our families and children were summed up in the work of Christ. Only then, will we see how God's steering hand used our fragile and frail efforts to accomplish his purposes in the world. Only then, after many have forgotten our name, will we hear from the Lord who has written our names in the book of Life: well done my good and faithful servant.

###### Conclusion

God's wisdom in the psalms is rich and rewarding. It not only offers us a blueprint for a godly household order, it also captures our spiritual imagination for a vibrant family life. The work of homebuilding is God-honoring work. In many respects it is a central and vital work in our larger lifework. The work of faithful homebuilding flourishes when marked by the fear of God, first by parents and then be children. God has given promises of blessing for faithful families and dutiful parents. But faithful building of hearth and home is meant to have an impact beyond itself influencing society, contending for the faith, impacting generations to come, and investing in eternity. <Callout>Done according to God's design, few vocations like Christian homebuilding make a greater impact in the world.</Callout> To this end, may we consider our calling as parents noble and fashion our family around God's grand and eternal purposes.

##### Session Summary

- Christian homebuilding is meaningful work. This work cannot be done without the Lord's help. The work of parenting is one of the most significant parts of our lifework.
- A parent's personal faith and devotion affects the way they go about their parenting work. Godly parents exemplify their devotion to their children in the way they go about their parenting work.

- God blesses the godly home. His shows his favor on godly families who fear God. Parents must tune their family to God's enduring blessings and give up the pursuit of temporary worldly pleasures.
- Parenting is a most important vocation vital for God's work in the world. Parents are to raise children so that they can be launched into the world in the service of God's will. Parents should raise their children to make a generational and global impact.

#### Charting the Path Ahead

*Reflect on the session and envision next steps. Record key takeaways from the lesson. Conclude your time by praying as small groups and a whole community. Review next steps.*

##### Final Review

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ChaPatAhe-FinRev-1">1. What key **takeaways**, **noteworthy observations**, or **biblical truths** most stood out to you during this session?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ChaPatAhe-FinRev-2">2. What **lingering questions** do you have about this session's topic?</Question>
<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ChaPatAhe-FinRev-3">3. What **personal applications** most challenged you? How do you most want to apply these teachings to your life?</Question>

##### Small Group Prayer

<Question id="Home-ParOnePre-SesSix-Ses6ComStu-ChaPatAhe-SmaGroPra-1">How can I pray for **other members** of my community?</Question>

##### Corporate Prayer

Gracious God, left to ourselves, we will fail at this great and noble work of parenting. We need your wisdom to guide us in the way of truth. We need your presence and power to enable us daily for this most important work. We need your grace to cover our sin, weakness, and insecurity. Make our family fit and faithful for your work. Establish our home in the service of your will. Fill our home with with favor and blessing. Make us fruitful and multiply the gospel through our children. Shape our children into sharpened arrows, ready to be launched into the world. Nurture our children like olive shoots, sincere in godly faith and bountiful in gospel fruit. What is built in our hearth and home, use as instruments for your eternal purpose. Help us Lord, we pray! Amen.

##### Next Steps

- Meet with a mentor to review this session.
- Memorize the biblical proverb.
- Complete the spiritual disciplines over the course of the week.
- Finish your personal and parenting project.

<< Psalm 139:23–24
